July 22nd, cont.

Have no desire for the lime-
light but may be forced into
it because of their gifts.
Like the other Cancer birth-
date, home conditions may in-
terfere with their freedom,
but not their mission. Absorb
their surroundings, so live
under great tension-- often
affecting the nerves. Should
have periods of aloneness to
recuperate. A card of inheri-
tance-- either by marriage or
from their own families. May
have periods of financial lim-
itation but should never have
to look for money. Are loyal,
devoted and self-sacrificing.
Great awareness of karmic con-
ditions and never resent them.
Are perfectionists in their
work. Talents are diversified
but music predominates; re-
markable technicians.

Aug. 20. Ruler-The Sun.

Leo.

In conflict with them-

selves between a desire

to serve without recompense
and a realization of the ne-
cessity for money as a means
of discharging obligations.
Sense of values uncertain and
may experience lack to a great~
er extent than other 6 C. If
they become materialistic are
bound to lose. Must be servers
or philanthropists. Should be
at the head of own business.
Less mental and can succeed

in commercial lines better
than others. Good lawyers, man-
ufacturers, bankers, real es-
tate operators. Can organize
charities, welfare movements,
etc. Valuable group members.

Sept. 18.Ruler- Mercury,

Vir.

Nervous, aloof, critical.

Want a reason for every-
thing they do; want to know
exactly what they're dealing
with, Inclined to live within
themselves. Resent intrusion
and criticism from others.

Oct.
Lib.

Nov.
Scor.

Dec.
Sag.

16.

14.

12,

Not usually well adapted for
marriage; work best alone.
Perfectionists in their work
and exacting with others.
Good statisticians, chart-
ists, detail workers. Too im-
patient for teaching. Should
cultivate faith and their in-
tuition; otherwise may be-
come selfish and penurious.
Give too much power to money.
Often seek seclusion through
a fear complex.

Ruler- Venus.

Both sexes are often dom-
inated by some woman. To
function happily, must have
appreciation. Highly emotion-
al, lovers of peace; will
make many compromises and
sacrifices to obtain it. May
get into a rut through fail-
ure to use their mental gifts,
Faithful and affectionate;
are messengers of peace,
Must strive to live positive-
ly and not fear to express
themselves. Too modest. Usu-
ally high minded and inter-
ested in humanitarian pro~
jects, Religiously inclined.
Ruler~ Mars.

Strong in will and emo-
tions. Intense and dram-
atic. Fixed ideas often in-
terfere with influence and
progress, Can commercialize
their talents and want suc-
cess. Demand action-~ no ruts.
As leader, can work well with
groups. Lawyers, actors, wri-
ters, inventors, The women
want a position of authority.
Ruler- Jupiter.

Want to make things work--
and pay. Must remain ac-

tive and productive. Public
spirited, progressive, Best
in a mental occupation--wri-
ting, teaching, lecturing.
Philosophical and broad-mind-
ed. Should develop any talent
for an emotional outlet; may
commercialize it.


## Page 98

SIX_OF DIAMONDS

Diamonds - Values

SD ~ Settlement of Karma

6 in D - Adjustment to Values,
Completion of Obligations.

The Mercury Card in the Jupiter L.
Displaces the 9 C in the Nat. Sp.

VALUES being the most import-
ant of all things for man to
learn and 6 being a number of set-
tlement and completion, it is evi-
dent that 6 D is the symbol of
all others for the balancing of
karmic debts. That this can be
done in the lifetime of these in-
dividuals is shown by the True
Place of the card-- the Jupiter
position in the Saturn Line. Sat-
urn represents the obligation,
Jupiter the blessing and reward.
The mundane position of the Birth
Card is at the head of the Jupit-
er Line-- Mercury-~ and we have
only to establish the right atti-
tude of mind (Mercury) to accept
the justice and necessity of the
6 D mission.

The acquisition of knowledge
is not easy for these people; the
displaced 9 C testifies to obsta~
cles and frustrations along ment-
al lines. There may be difficul-
ty in acquiring an education in
early life-- or there may be un-
willingness to bother with it on
the part of the natives. Money is
vital and they want to begin earn-
ing before they know where their
abilities lie or what sort of a
foundation they need to make a
success of it.

Saturn represents Obedience;
their first step in development
is to learn obedience to their own
Law. Early training is vital and
those who are handicapped by par
ents who are unable to administer

it must learn the hard way-- by
bitter experience and rigid self-
discipline. They must learn what
justice means; that every debt
demands payment and every obli-
gation must be discharged; that
strict and fearless honesty is
their portion and that nothing
less ever "pays off".

They are continually being
tested. Those who have a good
mental start pass the tests eas-
ily. They are natural mystics
and aspirants; they gravitate
toward religion and philosophy
and know which values are eter-
nal and which are not. They know
that their situation in life is
exactly what it should be-- for
it has been earned, for good or
ill. They recognize their miss-
ion and mean to fulfil it.

The others may learn late in
life-- but they do learn at last,
even though long established hab-
it interferes with application.

Finances may go to extremes-~
and remain in one state for a
long time-- up or down. In a long
period of "down", the unaware
ones may succumb to discourage-
ment and seek escape in drink or
drugs or dissipation. In these
cases the fight must be waged a-
gainst fear and for faith.

A very successful and satis-
factory life can be built when
money is not made the main object-
ive. The women should strive not
to depend upon their personalit-
ies for their success; the men
not to seek a wealthy marriage
for the sake of promoting their
own objectives. They have a know-
ledge of true values and must
share and distribute it-- or lose
it. Cause and Effect is their Law,

Planetary Sequence for the 6 D

Ven.
10 H

10 D

Good earning power is dev-
eloped early, but should
have a firm foundation. The
natural bent should be stud-
ied and a choice made that
will develop it, There may
be a disinclination to trav-
el, but it is an aid to bus-
iness. There is much innate
knowledge but it should be
regulated and classified if
it is to be retained. Par-
ents and home surroundings
are highly important. There
may be too much domination
by a possessive woman whose
influence may encourage neg~
ativity. The children of
these Birthdates should be
instilled with right princi-~
ples and then allowed to act
and think for themselves.
Make friends easily and
gain success through ne~
gotiations with congenial
people. Always involved with
the opposite sex. Are depen-
dent upon love and affection
and respond to it. Marriage
is often delayed until funds
are established. Engagements
are apt to be long. Care
should be taken not to arouse
jealousy or suspicion; these
people are subject to it and
may become victims of it.
Speculation is tabu--but

the temptation is often
present. This Card is in
the exact center of the
Spread--the Jupiter Card in
the Jupiter Line. In all act-
ivities (Mars) IF the right
sense of values is applied,
success is certain. By the
displacement of the Queen C
there is proof that Intuition
is the safest and surest
guide. Innate fairness makes
these people good judges and
honest dealers,

qj
n

AD

When applied to the realm

of labor, this is a suc~

cess card. 8 also brings ex-
pansion and progress and if

a good connection can be made
with a large organization or
a company employing many peo-
ple, power is built up by the
size and number. There is of-
ten a profitable connection
with railroads, labor groups
and manufacturing, Equal suc~
cess lies in the pursuit of

a religious vocation, teach-
ing or preaching the laws
they have come to uphold.

The sorrows and hardships

for these people assail
their emotions. Loss, separa-
tion or illness of loved ones
hit hard when they occur, for
love is ardently desired (AH)
and the satisfaction it might
bring is often denied. Grief
may also come through disap-
pointment in love-~-disillu-
sion or betrayal, and they
often become ill as a result,
There are instances of 6 D
women entering nunneries in
an attempt to forget their
personal tragedy and lose them-
selves in a higher form of love.
Harmony is essential to good
health and emotional disturb-
ance sometimes seriously im-
pairs it. These people are
good mental (not medical) heal-
ers and ardent sponsors and
benefactors of the underpriv-
ileged.

Desire for prominence and
importance in groups~~-es-
pecially those dealing with la-
bor problems. Want to stand
well and give the appearance
of plenty. Make sure that the
returns will be ample for any
effort expended. There is usu-
ally much correspondence con-
nected with these interests,
discussion of ideas, messages
and a wealth of detail.

Aug. 7.
bankers, theologians or writ- Leo.
ers employ novel and original
methods in their work. Very
progressive and influential.
Ruler- Venus.

Attract friends and are
helped by them. Are loyal
and generous, protective and
dependable. Stubborn and hard
to convince but can be won
over through affections. Will
work hard for results and for
money-~which is usually shar-
ed, The birthday number often
brings unforeseen trials--es-
pecially emotional. Fighters
for principle. Not personally
ambitious but will not spare
themselves in working for a
cause or an idea. Are child-
ren of nature; can succeed
in products of the earth or
dealing in commodities.
Ruler- Mercury.

Versatile and clever. Are
skilled musical technici-
ans--any occupation, in fact,
that requires nimble fingers.
Diversified interests. Choose
occupations connected with
travel or speaking. Can sell
by talking. Authorities on
data and statistics but sel-
dom have time or patience for
deep study. Can succeed in
commercial lines, but want a
quick turnover.

Ruler- The Moon.

Much concerned with ques-
tions affecting social con-
ditions, political economy
and international problems.
Usually traditional or reac-
tionary, but may be progress-
ive through the birthday num-
ber. Very humanitarian. Want
universal harmony and peace.
Not fighters as a rule but
have strong feelings and many
of the writers use a strong
pen. Interested in commodit-
ies for general use, household
helps, etc. May be lazy.

Sept. 5.
Vir.

Oct. 3.
Lib.

Nov. 1.

Scor.

Ruler- The Sun

Attracted to big enterpri-

ses and well advertised
ventures; never satisfied with
small returns. Large-minded,
big-hearted and generous,

Want power and publicity. Are
good actors, directors and
playwrights. Will not stay in
any business that does not ex-
pand rapidly and pay well.
Ruler- Mercury.

Intellectual and studious.
Feel they can never learn
enough so are never satisfied
with their knowledge. Want spi-
ritual contentment but are
skeptical and demand proof.
Apt to change type of work
through restlessness or a
sense of unfulfilment. Can
succeed in real estate or as
property managers. Composers-~
technical rather than inspi-
rational. Statesmen of the in-
tellectual type. Teachers of
science; writers, critics.
Ruler= Venus,

Expressive and emotional.
Fluent speakers and writ-

ers. Not always stable in af-
fections; apt to make experi-
ments in love-- usually be-
cause they are perfectionists.
Dramatic in their approach to
art, business or individuals,
Lovers of line, beauty and col-
or. May become very religious
in later life. Can succeed in
artistic or dramatic lines but
love is always more important
than money--or application to
their material interests. Are
successful in advertising or
radio.

Ruler- Mars.

Want to probe the myster-

ies. Many occult and meta-
physical students-~ or merely
interested in phenomena. Super-
stitious if undeveloped. Good
lawyers, metaphysicians or med-
ical doctors. Intense and dy-
namic; never lazy. Want money.

Yen.
10 ¢

-99-

F

Sequence for thi Ss

ro)
=)

The serious side of 6 S is
often balanced in youth by
association with gay and light-
hearted people, especially wom-
en. The mother is usually a
source of happiness or the sis-
ter may be kindly and affect-
ionate. Social gatherings, gay
parties and entertainments may
seem important and desirable
but they are soon abandoned
when maturity is reached. The
natural bent of these people
is serious and responsible,
but they are often given a
good start by the very con-
tacts they later dismiss as
trivial. Education is import-
ant and should be encouraged;
it is a big stepping stone in
later years.

The Venus, Mars and Jupiter
cards fall in the Crown

Line and the Venus influence
starts the development of pow-
er. If knowledge has not
hitherto been considered an
asset, the 10 C directs them
to seeking it and it becomes
a major satisfaction (Venus).
Success in this direction is
immediate; learning comes eas- KS
ily and as new doors are open-

ed their own self-confidence
develops and they begin to re-
alize that they are not the

tools of circumstance but are

the directors of their own

lives. Their attitude is posi-

tive -- and may be somewhat

stilted and ultra-dignified.

This may, of course, be over-

done and self-glorification

may result, Benefits come

suddenly and may be used un-

wisely, not recognized as

tests. The wise ones regard
themselves as custodians--not
owners. Lasting friends are

made and help is always at

hand. With the undeveloped,

the money may not last.

E

There are but four Birth-
dates in this group and

the reaction to the 8 D will
be different in each case.
Being Spades, however, the
natural tendency will be to
work for their objectives and
to make them pay. Here is the
indication that this can be
done~-especially if money is
not the sole aim. For all of
these people their power is
greatly increased by realiza-
tion that they are instru~
ments of Divine Will and that
they must keep in touch with
their Source. If 8 D is to
give them the key to true val-
ues, they must keep them-
selves in a state of aware-
ness for the instruction.
Every 6 S owes it to himself
to set apart a period each

day of his life for contact
with his Higher Self. His
knowledge must go beyond the
realm of the material; reli-
gion and philosophy must be-
come a vital part of his sci-
entific experiments, his art-
istic inspirations or his bus-
iness methods.

This is a card of great res-
ponsibility. If a man, he

is the builder of his own good;
if a woman, she will seek men
of importance and power. Both
are leaders in their own
spheres; both are in control of
their own situations. The neg-
ative or unaware will push oth-
ers aside for their own success;
they will seek domination rath-
er than leadership. However
they choose to act, there is
always power at their disposal
-- and the benefits it brings.
We see here both good and bad
leaders of labor groups; gree-
dy in free enterprise or phil-
anthropic in distributing its
returns. Instinctively they
know how to make things pay and
how to control their output.

7? SEVENS 7

EVEN is the most mystical of

all numbers, the hardest to
understand (and to live with) or
the most beautiful and rewarding
influence in anyone's life.

We have seen that it is the
center and foundation of the two
plans or Spreads in the "Little
Book"=- under the rulership of
the 7 Planets, built on the plan
of 7 rows down, 7 cards across-~
and set in the center of each
suit.

The 7th Card is the Neptune
Card, the 7th row the Neptune row,
which may account, in part, for
the confusion that arises in our
attempts to understand it. Nep-
tune is "extra-sensory'"-- and so
is 7, As soon as we use it on the
level of cold facts, mundane in-
terests and physical responsibil-
ities, we deprive ourselves of a
good half of its power if, in
thus using it, we lose sight of
its spiritual significance.

7 is called the dominical or
"holy" number, the Sabbath of rest
and pause to "see that all is good"
that is, perfect. It is this re-
quirement of perfection that we
can't quite live up to, the rest
and pause-for-examination to which
.we refuse to give the time. We
must therefore encounter the con~
fusions, obstacles and possible
defeat that Neptune invariably
bestows upon those who lack vis-
ion and have no concern for the
gifts of the spirit. The key is
found in the 7th Statement in the
Pattern on the Trestleboard--

"Living from that Will, support-
ed by its unfailing Wisdom and
Understanding, mine is the. Vic-
torious Life". As soon as we have
learned to live by that Will,
Wisdom and understanding, 7 will
bring us to Victory. On the Tree
of Life the 7th is the Sphere of
Victory.

For a better understanding of
the Divine Plan for the four 7's,
note the True Place of each--

HEARTS is the Neptune Card in the
Mercury Line. The ideal
of love is the right men-
tal attitude.

CLUBS is the Uranus Card in the
Mars Line. In the acquisi-
tion of knowledge intui-
tion is to be developed
and the channel opened for
inspiration.

DIAMONDS is the Saturn Card in
the Saturn Line-~ a warn-
ing to use strict self-dis-
cipline in estimating true
values.

SPADES is the Jupiter Card in the
Neptune Line. This is the
sure reward of the seeker
after the "higher realm"
wisdom.

7 is the number of the soul.
In silence, peace and self-exam-
ination we go toward "perfection".
In criticism of others, suspicion,
judgment on face-value and sharp
practice we create our own obsta-
cles and invite our own difficul-
ties, There are no "young souls"
with a 7 Birth Card. All know
that theirs is the quest for Truth.

Sequence for the 7 H

Finances are usually limit-
ed in early life (note the
two 7's in proximity). Loss-
es are unforeseen and unex-
pected demands are made on
the resources, It is not safe
to take chances or gamble but
the inclination is there. In
education there are obstacles
encountered, in work there is
seldom adequate payment, in
love there is frustration and
expense. Money is spent read-
ily-- usually for self,

Home may seem burdensome

and the desire for escape
incites to travel and a vari-
ety of experience. The love
of home remains, however, and
they always want to return to
it. To home they usually re-
main loyal; it is only in the
personal relationships that
instability is evident. They
want love but the inclination
to suspicion and jealousy des-
troys it. Once these people
find themselves and settle
down, love has a chance to
come and stay. Sociability
and hospitality are natural;
they want to live well and en-
joy entertaining.

This is the sacrifice card
and if there is no inclin-
ation in that direction, it
will be replaced by self-pity.
The attitudes are fixed but
they may be strongly influ-
enced by some friend or
member of the family. Through
this influence an inclination
toward religion may be devel-
oped and they may become mar~
tyrs to their work; they must
be convinced, however, that
the cause in which they are
interested is a worthy one or
they won't stay with it. In
any suit Jacks can be frivo-
lous and time-wasting.

E

iv)
a

in

rv)
a

ic

nN

Many of the business diffi-
culties are caused by a lack
of sound educational founda-
tion. Some disappointing ex-
periments may be made before
the best type of business is
found. They are most attract~
ed to something that is stim-
ulating and adventurous; rou-
tine is distasteful and rare-
ly contributes to success.
Unless poise has been acquired
through spiritual development
there is much restlessness in
this card and the natives need
push and incentive in order to
follow a given course. Care
must be taken to establish
friendly relations with employ~
ees; loss and imposition may
come from that source,

Any illness-- contracted or
congenital-- may be linger-
ing and difficult to diagnose.
Although interested in chemi-
cals and drugs, they are usu-
ally averse to taking medi-
cines themselves. Their own
state of health or the active
illness of some member of the
family may interfere with bus-
iness or personal plans. They
like to investigate and exper-
iment in cures and prevent-
ives-- but not on themselves.
The mind is usually keen and
there is often an uncanny ab-
ility in mathematics.

Work in groups is best

and whatever its nature,

it should always be in close
cooperation with some one
else-- a person of high intel-
ligence preferably. There is
a tendency to shift responsi-
bility so a careful selection
should be made when it comes
to any close partnership.
Work interests will proceed
smoothly if a spirit of har
mony and friendship is pre-
served. In all dealings an
adviser should be on hand.

Birthdates

-104-

(Note that we have left

the Venus L; now in Mars).
The desire to become a lead-
er or owner seems to increase
with the years, but there is
always some uncertainty re-
garding what course to take.
They want to travel and usu-
ally leave the place of birth,
often establishing a perma-
ment residence at a distance.
The November birthdate espe-
cially is attracted to the
sea and may want to own his
own ship. The majority want
to be near the water. Unless
there is some obligation that
prevents it, these people of-
ten become rovers in the la~
ter years.

c e i H
JEALOUSY

led by the 7 H

Sept. 30.Ruler- Venus.

Lib.

Oct. 28.
Scor.

Must guard against self-
indulgence, laziness and
selfishness. Want to shine
in their chosen work-- as
star and benefactor. Like to
live in ease and comfort but
often have to work hard for
success. Love affairs are in-
tense while they last. There
is much talent in this birth-
date and ability to succeed
independently if the talent
is cultivated and an artist-
ic or dramatic line chosen.
If they go into business
they need cooperation and
guidance. Are good talkers
and make excellent trial law-
yers. Can also engage in ad-
vertising, publishing and
(in some cases) banking.
Ruler- Mars

Have fixed ideas-- and
devotion to them. Cannot

be talked out of an opinion

Nov.
Sag.

Dec,
Cap.

26.

24.

once formed. Subject to acci-
dents that may interfere with
their work. May have sudden
breaks or climaxes in their
lives, long-lasting illness-
es or a chronic condition, in-
herited or acquired. More du-
tiful and self-sacrificing than
the other 7 H birthdates, (of-
ten needlessly), and seldom ap~
preciated. Given to unconven-
tional unions. Must guard a-
gainst escape from discour-
agement through drink or drugs.
May be strongly attracted to
occultism and change the
whole course of their lives.
If so, become active in secret
orders. Are seekers for truth.
Succeed as teachers, lectur-
ers or writers. If not inter-
ested in the mysteries are
apt to follow engineering, me-
chanics-~ or undertaking.
Ruler- Jupiter.

Intellectual and practical--
but also endowed with imag-
ination and a sense of poetry.
Nervous and restless-- actual-
ly seeking peace and poise.
Should seek an occupation in
the field of education, liter-
ature or philosophy--anything
that taxes their fine mental
capacity. Clever (often gift-
ed) at working in bronze, tin
or marble. Money does not come
easily and should be budgeted.
Should have frequent sojourns
in the country-- alone.

Ruler- Saturn.

Highly ambitious. More self-
sufficient than the rest,
Dignified and self-important.
Critical and easily offended.
Serious-minded and responsi-
ble. Should never retire; need
constant activity. Should av-
oid connection with hospitals,
institutions of confinement.
Can succeed in business or as
trustees, government officials
or public administrators.


## Page 109

SEVEN _OF CLUBS

fe)

lubs - Knowledge

Le - Worry re Accomplishment,

7_in C - Spiritual Power in Rev-
elation.

The Uranus Card in the Saturn L.

Displaces the 8 D in the Nat. Sp.

Pe)

This card never lacks the in-
spiration of Uranus, as its True
Place is also in the Uranus posi-
tion (Mars Line). We have the 3
rulerships to consider-- Saturn
for the Line, Uranus for the po-
sition and Mars for the True
Place. Saturn will always make
trouble for us if we disregard
his laws, and thus it is with
the 7 C. Instead of cultivating
their great gift of intuition
and listening for their instruc-
tion, they too often succumb to
the Saturn pressure, accept dis-
couragement (or rail against the
obstacles in their path) and wor-
Ty over a multitude of things
that never happen.

The displaced 8 D assures
them of the power behind them--
a power that not only gives them
an opportunity to exercise right
judgment of values but secures
their protection when discrimin-
ation is exercised. The Mars ru-
lership of the True Place says,
Work for it, fight for it if ne-
cessary but USE it at all costs.
These people can always make mon-
ey (their chief worry) if they
will work for it. Many of them
do work, but periodically they
get into a panic and plunge into
some unwise investment or get-
rich-quick scheme which leaves
them poorer than ever.

Much of the trouble lies in
a lack of preparation. Being in
the realm of Clubs, a thorough
education is the prime essential,

When this is neglected they get
off to a bad start, as far as ac-
complishment is concerned. Some
periods of financial limitation
are bound to come and they need
trained minds and well stocked
brains to combat them,

As with all 7's, there is a
subconscious urge for spiritual de-
velopment. The 7 C wants proof and
tangibility and when that is not
forthcoming they abandon the par-
ticular creed or code they have
been experimenting with and try
another, If their state of mind
about religion is sufficiently
troubled, they will keep on seek-
ing until they find a faith to
cling to.

The men of this card should
strive to work under the K C; in
that Sequence the answers to his
problems will come more readily.

There is sometimes scandal and
backbiting connected with this
card-- especially for those who
waste their time and substance and
scatter their energies. Trouble in
their work usually comes through
labor disputes and unreliable em-
ployees, This often reacts unfav-
orably on their health, increasing
their natural nervousness and men-
tal confusion. They must realize
that they can succeed-~ and splen~
didly-- through work and applica~
tion. They must shun petty and
frivolous associates, psychic ex-
periments, gambling, drink and
careless, thoughtless living.

Those who are "right side up"
(and there are many) have provided
themselves with a fine education-
al foundation, have developed
their intuitional power and have
crowned their lives with splendid
achievement and success.

If their problems have

been honestly wrestled

with and good judgment gain-

Challenge for the 7 C
AGNOSTICISM

ss Ruled by the 7 C

29, Ruler~ Mars.

The mental attitude must

be kept clear and strong--

no negativity. These people
often suffer from the machin-
ations of others and become
embittered and easily discour-
aged. Should stick to a course
and not give up. Clever and
inventive. Good draughtsmen,
mechanical engineers, archi-
tects, surveyors. May be con-
nected with law or politics,
If in a commercial line, suc-
ceed best with metals, machin~
ery, sharp instruments. The
women often make good nurses,
laboratory technicians or ex-
perts in home economics.

Apr. 27. Ruler- Venus

Tau.

Helped by women-- but not
romantically involved with
them. The men are more apt to
become attached to those who
are not helpful, but more glam-
ourous. Are naturally intui-
tive. Love music and should
cultivate some artistic line
as an outlef€ for their emo-
tions. May be dominated by con-
ditions at home or by the mo-

May 25.
Gem.

June 23.
Can.

ther. Are more at peace when
living close to the earth.
Should strive to eliminate
fear of insecurity. May gain
@ position of authority which
dispels their fears. May be
interested in social and pol-
itical and prison reform.
Have a more universal view-
point than many 7 C and are
usually well educated and well
balanced. Are studious and
philosophical. May attain a
high place in government ser-
vice. Good writers-- usually
along serious lines, ~ history,
philosophy, etc.

Ruler- Mercury.

The majority of these peo-

ple are doubting Thomases.
Very talkative and self-ex-
pressive by nature, but sel-
dom reveal their true senti-
ments on any subject. This
subtlety may give them an oc-
casional advantage in busi-
ness but does not help their
personal relationships. They
like to sound people out and
agree to whatever is popular
or expedient. Will never com-
mit themselves without keep-
ing an ace in the hole. Are
interested in the races, in
business involving transport-
ation or anything that moves
rapidly and frequently changes.
The more developed and educat-
ed often go to the other ex-
treme and become deep thinkers,
philosophers or psychologists.
For them writing is the most
important field of influence,
Those who are less exceptional
can succeed as lawyers, agents,
salesmen or auctioneers.
Ruler- The Moon.

(This birthdate may fall

in the last degree of Gem.

but it is rare). Restless and
ambitious but not always sure
of themselves, They need en-
couragement and affection. In

July 21.
Can.

~108-

certain directions, however,
they have strong opinions
and firm convictions and for
these they will go to any
lengths to uphold. Of all the
7 C they are the most depen-
dent upon affection and most
devoted to those they love.
They want to shine as spon-
sors of the underprivileged
but their timidity keeps
them in the background. Are
disturbed about lack of mon-

with what they have. They are
idealistic, poetical and mu~
sical but cannot commercial-
ize the arts. They make good
managers of apartment houses
and hotels, good caterers
and successful dealers in
household commodities. They
often like to follow the sea
or live close to it. Can deal
in liquids-- especially per-
fumes.

Ruler- The Moon.

Much more self-assertive

and self-promotive than

the other Cancer birthdate.
Like the limelight and are
attracted to the stage or
platform, whether talented
or not. Many playwrights and
actors are found in this date;
also singers, musicians and
lecturers. The women are es-
pecially gifted in clothes de-
signing, running dress shops
or executing orders for inter-
ior decorations. Like display
and are clever in creating
it. Work best when they

have an appreciative audi-
ence. Influenced by home and
family. Usually have a home
that is artistic and in good
taste. Want cooperation but
are unusually independent--
for Cancer. Must avoid sel-
fishness and a critical ten-
dency. Like to have others
dependent upon them. Are gen-
erous and protective.

Aug. 19. Ruler- The Sun
Leo. Self-confident and highly
ambitious. Aspire to a po-
sition of authority in what-
ever line they follow. When
they have learned tolerance
and developed a humanitarian
spirit, become valuable lead-
ers-- but this usually is de-
layed until they are advan-
ced in years. Must have prom-
inence and excitement, so many
are attracted to the theatre
-- and often make a success
of it. Better for the stage
then the movies for they pre-
fer to be their own directors.
If in a commercial line,
should be at the head of the
business. Strong supporters
of law and order. Reactionary.
Original and creative. Good
merchandisers, customs house
brokers or government offi-
cials. Always dramatic.
Sept. 17.Ruler- Mercury.
Vir. Can drive sharp bargains.
Should cultivate breadth
of viewpoint in money matters
and avoid pettiness and penu-
riousness. Good tax experts,
accountants, technicians. Ef-
ficient and thorough in draw-
ing up documents, legal pa-
pers (briefs) and trust deeds;
mever miss a point. Dislike
limitation but do not exert
themselves to eliminate it.
Have periods of generosity
and extravagance. Should try
to eliminate ulterior motives.
Ruler- Venus.
Love art, music, poetry-~
and beauty. Strong reli-~
gious inclinations-- not usu-
ally orthodox, Like ceremony
and "setting" with their reli-
gion. Usually endowed with a
strong humanitarian urge and
will use their talents to pro-
mote culture, education and
general welfare. Will become
actors to “elevate the stage"
or marry to reform the mate.

Lib.

fDi - Conflict between Spir- the 7 D is the Saturn Card in
it and Matter. the Saturn Line; and the 9 H is
7 in D ~- Peace through Victory. the Venus Card in the Venus Line.

The Venus Card in the Venus L.
Displaces the 9 H in the Nat. Sp.

These two cards are inextrica-
bly linked together. In all of the
90 quadrations they exchange places
and are never found elsewhere. One
or the other is always the Venus
card in the Venus Line or the Sat-
urn Card in the Saturn Line. You
will note, too, that the True Place

accept their crosses as log-
ical results of their ow
causes and set about dis-
charging their karmic debts
willingly, they become truly

great people-- and the cross-

es miraculously disappear.
They are gifted as writers,
healers, teachers, metaphy-
sicians and philosophers.

This should say much to the
student who has gone thus far in
the study of the Sacred Symbols.
7's represent material or personal
difficulties OR spiritual victory;
9's represent personal disappoint-
ment and frustration OR peace and
fulfilment through universal love.

KH

-lll-

There are problems here,

as a rule, but none that
cannot be surmounted by those
in full command of themselves
and endowed with a sense of
true values. Concentration
and hard work are sure to re-
sult in achievement. Business
is not always productive with-
out a long preliminary strug-
gle. If they work entirely a-
lone there are losses; a lev-
el-headed partner is a great
asset to them. If there is an
inheritance, there is usually
trouble with the will or con-
test from other beneficiaries.
The inheritance may be disap-
pointing or money spent to
collect it.

There is some connection

with illness- usually of

a loved one, although the wom-
en often become visiting nur-
ses, and efficient ones. In
both sexes there is an inner
desire for contact with anoth-
er plane-- which may or may
not be disregarded. Under

this influence a strong reli-
gious interest may be devel-
oped and may turn them sudden-
ly to a type of work that chan-
ges their entire lives. Care
should be taken to avoid acci-
dents for themselves and they
are often involved with acci-
dents of ethers, If a woman,
marriage may be interfered
with through family responsi-
bility. Some form of sacri-
fice is a requirement for
this Birth Card.

There is strong psychic

power here and a desire

for other-plane knowledge.

If developed, this is a great
asset in service to others--
and priceless for themselves.
These people are kindly em-
ployers and are much concern-
ed with the welfare of those
in the ranks of labor. They

al
Qi
Sk

become leaders of groups or
fraternities that are work-
ing for progress and improve-
ment-- especially after 45.
These people are naturally
clairaudient and should de-
velop their gift. If working
mainly on the material plane
will do much traveling in la-
ter life-- and usually have
the means at their command.
They are attracted to the wa-
ter-- some profession con-
nected with the sea or sea~
travel or the establishment
of their own homes near a
body of water. Although dev-
elopment may be delayed,
these natives are capable of
greatness and often become
justly famous,

THE HARMONIZATION OF MONEY AND LOVE

Birthdates Ruled by the 7 D

Jan. 20.
Cap.

Feb. 18.
Aquar.

Ruler- Saturn

Money may be accumulated,

but rarely is except by

hard work. There is a certain
sternness and rigidity in
these people that does not
deny friendliness but seldom
evinces any sympathy. Make
good, hard-headed physicians,
courteous but unbending ambas-
sadors or diplomats. The other
side of the picture is selfish,
over~ambitious and a climber.
Influenced by the personali-
ties of others but seldom show
it. Can succeed as labor lead-
ers or property managers. If
aware of the inspiration in
the birthday Number, can suc~
cessfully cultivate some lat-
ent talent and commercialize it.

Demand personal freedom

but have a desire for ser-
vice. If a man, eager for move~

July 8.
Can.

Aug. 6.
Leo.

-113-

Ruler- The Moon.

Acquisitive and self-prot-
ective-- through fear of
lack. Want money badly but
cannot always keep it; self-
indulgent spenders. Like to
be prominent in the community
and appear well-to~do. Will
contribute to projects but
want their names at the top
of the list. Apt to be lazy
but will work if there is a
chance to accumulate. Are of-
ten gifted along artistic
lines and should cultivate any
latent talent; this brings out
the best of them. If make a ca-
reer of business, may become
ruthless and penurious. Those
who are less money~conscious
become active in commmity,
church or general welfare pro-
jects.

Ruler- The Sun.

A difficult birthdate un-
less dedicated to service.

In this case money is apt to
be a problem, but sacrifice
is cheerfully accepted. The
usual Aug. 6 people are the
most monied of all the 7 D;
they are either born to money
inherit it or marry it.

In that case, the personal
life leaves much to be de-
sired. Have many opportuni-
ties but seldom embrace them.
Will spend lavishly on home
and personal comfort. Need to
be loved for themselves but
are usually sought for their
money. When these people be-
come truly philanthropic and
eager to share their wealth,
they stand a fine chance of

Sept. 4.
Vir.
Oct. 2.
Lib.

personal peace and happiness.
The usual picture is one of
boredom, loneliness-- and an
accumulation of ailments.
Succeed best in a large busi-
ness-- banking, brokerage or
manufacturing. May be good
lawyers, actors or directors.
Ruler- Mercury.

Must work hard to attain a
key position. Apt to be
meticulous and fussy, swamped
with detail. The mind is keen
but critical; their very men-
tality may become a burden.
Must avoid worry and fretful-
ness. Very successful at re-
search and technical details.
Also well adapted for real
estate, commodities-- especi-
ally groceries--merchandising
and selling small articles.
Can teach or write if other
factors in the chart are sup-
porting.

Ruler- Venus.

This is the most artistic
and gifted of all the 7 D.
Great painters belong to this
birthdate, actors and compo-
sers. To the majority, art
and beauty come first. Inter-
ested in foreign countries and
foreign travel. Good foreign
agents, diplomats and ambas-
sadors. If not artistically
inclined, should study law.
May become strongly religious
and universally-minded. Have
high ideals and great influ-
ence over others. May become
too self-effacing and sacrifi-
cial for their own good. If
not well balanced mentally
may have a martyr complex.

Planeta

Merc.

a

={15
Sequence the Ss

In youth the reactions are
quick and argumentative.

They feel on the defensive--
partly from a desire to learn
quickly, partly from fear that
they cannot accomplish all
that is expected of them. Are
good students and good debat-
ers. Throughout life they are
"joiners" and they start early.
They are subject to sudden in-
terruptions or calls in vari-
ous directions. They are re-
garded as errand boys-- or
girls-- and are constantly at
the beck and call of others.
Are attracted to those of
strong mental power. A well 2s
educated man-- relative or not
-- may have a great influence.
The women are apt to marry an
older man who is in a mental
type of work. Very seldom at-
tracted to frivolity. The emo-
tions are deep and lasting but
emotional relationships are
built more on respect and ad-
miration than on demonstration.
Very capable at handling ac-
counts and finances for oth-
ers. Absolutely trustworthy.
Often found in charitable or hu-
manitarian organizations-- Red
Cross, Boy Scouts, etc.-- and
usually behind the scenes. Are
humble and self-effacing but no
door-mats. Will work very hard
to get things done-~ with or
without remuneration. Keep their
private lives and business well
separated. Legal minds.
Interested in living well

and enjoy making enough mon-

ey to make it possible. They
seldom have to struggle for a
good living unless the early ed-
ucation has been much neglected.
The pleasure connected with mak-
ing money is less materialistic
than in most cases; they want

it for what it brings rather

Sat.
4D

than for pride of possession.
Benefits come through travel,
especially by water. They are
good mixers and firm friends.
In case of any illness of

self or family, they are
assured of good care and am-
ple funds. Great believers

in preserving the health and
are strong for preventive and
natural methods. Usually live
long and remain useful and ac-
tive. If they have a health
or physical affliction are un-
complaining and resigned. They
never forget to count their
blessings and always feel they
are many.

Cooperative and work well

in partnership. Believe

in benefits and privileges for
employees. Often leaders of
welfare groups, better housing
committees, etc. Are good exe-
cutives. Work well with any-
thing connected with the land.
Are kindly and diplomatic.
Good agents, negotiators, etc.
If they have been serious

and much occupied in early
life and the middle years, they
take more time for sociability
when they are older. Life is
usually well protected and ve-
ry pleasant. They seldom re-
tire from active work because
the sense of power is increas-
ed rather than diminished.
Time and money are spent in
philanthropic enterprises and
they seldom want credit for
the gifts and benefits they
bestow. If they have failed to
overcome their obstacles in
the earlier years, they usual-
ly can before they die.

## Page 121

EIGHTS

J bese are the Power Cards.
Some of the early mystery
schools taught that 8 was

the number of God and that its

use by man would bring him evil.
From this superstition the prac-
tice arose, among many of the old-
school numerologists, of assign-
ing to 8 the rulership of Saturn
as the embodiment of evil. Today
we know-- both from experience
and from the Higher Teaching--
that 8 is the number of the Sun

(and therefore of God) and that

Saturn is not the embodiment of

evil.

Our mathematical symbol for
infinite measure or "infinity" is
the horizontal 8 and this same
symbol, as "all power" is over
the head of the Magician in the
Tarot and of the woman in the 8th
card-- Strength-- who is opening
the lion's jaws with her hands.

When we come to look upon
wealth as the symbol of power and
write our 8's with a very small
loop at the top and a very large
one below then, of course, 8 may
bring us evil and money may just-
ly be called its root. It is actu-
ally a picture of God's circle of
power above reflected in man's be-
low.

In the cards we find several
geometrical figures of repeated 4's
-- two squares, 8 triangles, two
tetrads, two right angles, etc--
the security of 4 doubled, or the
intimation that upon a firm foun-
dation may be built another of
greater power and expansion. 8 is
the first free number, for it comes

at the "turn" of the 7's. It is the
"Eternal Splendor of the Limitless
Light". (pattern on the Trestle-
board).

The natives of these cards
can expand in any direction-- ac-
cording to their will and the
outlines of their pattern. The
Bower is always with them. They
may turn the power to evil uses
if they choose (and there are
many 8's who operate very nega-
tively indeed) but they are free;
they reflect God's Plan but they
are not bound by it.

HEARTS have the power to harmon-
ize their lives, increase
their resources and expand
their field of service
through Love-- personal,
universal and Divine.

CLUBS have the power to acquire
knowledge-- and the obli-
gation to disseminate it.
If they will not learn
and teach they cannot ful-
fil their mission. They
must follow the admonition
of St. Peter to “add know-
ledge to your faith".

DIAMONDS have the power to acquire
wealth-- and the obligation
to share it. The "Limitless
Substance" is at their dis-
posal, twice over. They are
"crowned", therefore custo-
dians and trustees. They
represent the bank of spir-
itual and material security

SPADES have the power to acquire
true wisdom and to live un-
der God's Laws. Symbols of
death, they are free to dis-
prove its reality.

Planetary Sequence for the 8 H

Unless working under the
Personality Cards, the

early life may be monotonous
but is usually well protect-
ed and harmonious. The ment-
al equipment is good but not
in the "prodigy" class. In-
sight and intuition are dev-
eloped early. They resist
changes and like to remain

in one place for a long time.
There is a slow but steady
increase in the desire for
knowledge. Can always over-
come any obstacles that stand
in the way of acquiring an
education.

Emotional problems and dis-
appointments can be over-
come through the power in this
card-- although some early ex-
perience in love may be, for
a time, very devastating. If
a love or friendship is once
formed, they want it to last
"forever". The women of these
dates want travel-- and usual-
ly have it-- but home roots
are strong and a home of their
own-- not parental-- is much
desired. Unless working under
the Personality Card, in the
case of women there are apt to Uran.
be long engagements. Both sexes K S
want money that is sufficient
and ample security,

If a woman, this Mars Card

is also her Personality

and she is much influenced by
it-- especially in relations
with the opposite sex. All
Heart natives like amusement
and diversion-- the Q H more
than the rest. This can be a
very frivolous and flirtatious
individual and the power in
the card can be hopelessly dis-
sipated. If working positively,
the women are faithful, mother-
ly and warm-hearted and may
overdo the mother-love complex.
The men may be dominated by

od
sk

ey
Io
Ir

re)
o

=e
io
US

the wife or mother, but pre-
fer the society of strong-
minded women and are often
materially helped by them.

It is important to note

that this "blessing" card

is in the Crown Line-- prov-
ing that the real benefits

in these lives come from on
high. Power is given to ap-
ply what they know-- and if
there has been a good educa-~
tional background, much can be
accomplished in the ment-

al field. There is an in-
born sense of true knowledge
and mental pursuits are like-
ly to be the most lucrative.
Their gift of understanding
gives them success in deal-
ing with others.

The necessity for making
money may entail hard work,
but the objective is usually
accomplished. Possibility of
an inheritance or gain of
some sort through goods of
the dead. Money can be made
through healing or a connect~-
ion with hospitals or rest
homes. There is usually a
good health foundation but it
may be disrupted through care-
lessness.

Ability to control others

-- especially employees.

Work best where large numbers
of people are employed. Will
champion causes that benefit
society. Not well adapted for
menial work. Good executives.
Are found as leaders and dir-
ectors of large groups. If
drawn to a religious career,
make fine missionaries-- med-
ical or spiritual-- especial-
ly in the foreign field. May
be sponsors of religious move-
ments or institutions.

Unless there has been much
spiritual development and
understanding of the pattern,
the emotional life may be
more disturbed in the later

## Page 125

EIGHT OF CLUBS

Clubs - Knowledge
c - Power in Knowledge

in_C - Material Mastery through
the Power of Mind.

joo

The Neptune Card in the Mars L.
No displacement. This is one of
the fixed cards and remains in
the same position in both spreads.

Neptune holds the key to this
card and the Mars "conjunction"
either sharpens its power-value
or destroys it.

The mixture of mental strength,
spiritual awareness, psychic power
and powerful emotions is sometimes
too much for these people to han-
dle and dire confusion is the re-
sult. When the psychic power is
extreme (as in some cases), unless
great care is taken for protection,
they become fields for possible in-
vasion. They should strive at all
times for mental balance and not
allow their emotions, their fixed
ideas or tendency to temperament
to dominate them. The charts (as-
trological and numerological) of
the children of these dates should
be carefully studied for any men-
tal support along practical lines
and these points strengthened in
the early years. There is no fi-
mer material to be found anywhere
than in the 8 C equipment, but it
must be guarded and guided.

Set principles and fixed ment-
al attitudes have been "brought
over" and from these they cannot
be swerved. When they are able to
clarify their objectives, they al-
ways go straight toward them-- and
attain them. Through the power of
knowledge, which is their heritage,
they can overcome any obstacle and
attain any desire. Their entire
Planetary Sequence is in the Jup-

iter line and protection surrounds
them in all departments of life.

Being a member of the trinity
of fixed cards, they are allied
with the wisdom of the K S and the
sacrifice of the J H. They, too,
are on the cross-- as is often ver-
ified in their emotional lives.

The majority have an avid de-
sire for knowledge and allow noth-
ing to interfere with its pursuit.
They have come to teach and they
intend to equip themselves for it.
They work better with large groups
than with individuals or small cir-
cles. The greater numbers seem to
generate additional power.

If they form any alliance with
J H or K S or become attached to
any natives of these birthdates,
an expansive force is produced
that is far-reaching and cannot
be broken.

They should adhere strictly
to their own birthcard and never
attempt to operate under the per-
sonality; if they do, they lose
much of their power.

On the negative side these
people may amount to nothing what-
ever-- having no awareness of the
extent of their influence or the
power invested in them. On the
destructive side they can, if they
choose, reverse this power and be-
come black magicians.

Unless very strong and sure

of themselves, they should avoid
psychic phenomena. They are actu-
ally in close touch with the high-
er planes and have no concern with
the astral. Danger lies there-- and
the possibility of invasion. They
have been given an important com-
mission and must adhere to it.

Challenge for the 8 C

FEAR OF DOMINATION

Birthdates Ruled by the 8 C

Mar. 28.
Aries.

Apr. 26.
Tau.

May 24.

Ruler- Mars.

Impulsive and dynamic.

Lack vision and seldom

stop to consider the final
results of their actions.
Argumentative-- often quar-
relsome. Capacity for deep
affection-- and need it--

but are undiplomatic and un-
intentionally inconsiderate.
Impatient with stupidity. Al-
ways disturbed emotionally.
Succeed best with men-- in
politics, law, partnerships,
that involve questions of
judgment. Very restless and
"Martian". May be gifted in
art or music but better suit-
ed to business.

Ruler- Venus.

Build constructively for

the future. Desire a home

and will work for it. Want

to stand well with others and
are disturbed by inharmony.
Often marry for money for the
sake of security. Generous if
they have the means. Prefer
connection with large enter-
prises-- manufacturing, bank-
ing, produce merchandising.
Are often artists or musicians
and if they lack talent for
success, still want the outlet
and take it up as a hobby. Can
succeed also in the education-
al field and welfare projects.
Ruler- Mercury.

Interested in people and
curious about them. Experi-
mental and brilliant-- some-
times erratic and wholly irre-
sponsible, Natural gamblers
because interested in results
but seldom win. If willing to
cultivate a sense of responsi-
bility and conquer the tenden-

June 22.
Gem. or
Can.

July 20,
Can.

Aug. 18.
leo.

cy to scatter their forces,
can become great teachers,
leaders, preachers and arbi-
trators. The women like to
establish "salons" and bring
noted people together.
Rulers- Mercury and Moon
This birthdate usually

falls in Cancer but may
occur in the last degree of
Gemini. Seldom find them-
selves until middle life.

In the early years are unde-
cided and vacillating. When
settled in a career are eag~
er to impart their knowledge
to others. Must exercise
self-discipline and culti-
vate emotional stability.
Can succeed in medicine,
nursing or any line that im-
proves the physical condi~
tion. Keenly mental and in-
tuitive. Women succeed well
with home economics, dress
shops (or dressmaking) or
teaching. In both sexes the
gift of writing may be out-
standing.

Ruler- The Moon.

Successful in public life
and working for humanity.
May get into a rut through
laziness. Can become leaders
in politics or religion, Are
patient and make successful
teachers of children. Good
counselors and judges-- es-
pecially in domestic rela-
tions. Interested in child
welfare and reform. If musi-
cally talented, can commer-
cialize it. Give good advice
but don't follow it them-
selves.

Ruler- The Sun.

Have a great drive for pow-
er and the limelight. Must
be at the head of own busi-
ness; cannot work for others
May become famous in their
chosen line. Successful in
connection with banking, ad-
ministration of wills and

## Page 129

EIGHT OF DIAMONDS

Diamonds - Values
&D - Substantial Success
8 in D ~- Material Control

The Central Card in the Crown L.
Displaces the Q S in the Nat. Sp.

All eights are power, but it
is the 8 D that surpasses the oth-
ers in material power. Its posi-
tion in the Crown Line not only
denotes its high calling but en-
dows it with greater freedom of
choice than is possessed by any
of the cards below that Line. As
noted above, (see p. 13) all the
Crown Cards are granted Movable
Choice and can operate in any po-
sition that best suits their re-
quirements, This freedom makes the
8 D people very independent-- at
times domineering and exacting.
The displacement of the Q S only
increases this tendency, for Q S$
natives, while willing to work
and to serve are always conscious
of their position of rulership.

The face-arrangement of all
8's denotes balance; again the 8
D surpasses the rest by being in
the exact center at the top. The
sense of balance is naturally di-
rected to values and they usually
know when and what to buy and what
it is worth-- exactly.

As in all cases, their power
is used or misused. They can be
philanthropic or mercenary, bene-
factors or misers, universally-
minded or self-servers. When they
choose to operate negatively, the
inevitable result is suffering
and tragedy. For many the re-
quirement is too exacting-- or it
may be unrecognized. They may not
know that their Birth Card is the

Sun Card and that they are direct
emissaries of the Central Sun.
But the soul knows-~ and if they
take the time and trouble to be-
come acquainted with their own
souls, they will be told.

They are the manifestation of
the creative principle, closely
associated with the resurrection
and the certainty of re-birth.
Theirs is the gift of sublimation,
theirs the ability to overcome
all obstacles and conquer all en-
emies. The majority are well aw-
are of the heavy responsibilities
and are willing to discharge them.
If this is not realized in youth,
recognition comes after 36. As a
rule, trust and confidence may be
freely given them, They are wise
guardians of the goods of the
dead and wise conservers of the
interests of the living. They
will serve honestly and faithful-
ly, often at their own expense.

The main pitfalls are love
of power (and a certain ruthless-
ness in exercising it) and love
of the money that enhances it.
They may be thrown completely off
balance by worshiping the golden
calf, forget their obligations,
spend the inheritance entrusted to
them and swiftly accomplish their
own downfall and disgrace. "Those
who rise high, fall hard". Their
place is already high-- and they
have the strength in their wings
to keep them there.

To fulfill their destiny they
need not be financial magnates or
kings of industry, They may be the
mother who sacrifices, the teacher
who opens doors of understanding
or the professional man who helps
the client in need-- without pay.

“127-

Challenge for the 8 D
MONEY AS POWER

Birthdates Ruled by the 8 D

Jan. 19. Ruler- Saturn.

Cap.

Feb.
Aquar

Mar.
Pisc,

17.

is.

The women are successful
managers of home and fam-
ily; can always make both
ends meet. In any occupation
efficiency is stressed. Am-
bitious to be the best of
their kind. Men succeed as
heads of their own business.
Often choose merchandising
that furnishes supplies for
scientists or professionals.
A karmic number. Must be
strictly just and fair. Not
always satisfied in the per-
sonal life, Unusual streak
of poetry and mysticism for
Capricorn. Have high ideals.
Ruler- Uranus.

Original methods in busi-
ness or profession. Full

of unusual ideas. Intuitive
and inventive. Always mental
in attitude. Usually have a
strong inclination to reli-
gion-- their own brand. Be-
lieve in universal good will.
If operating negatively, can
be cruel and vindictive.
Succeed as writers, scient-
ists, managers of large en-
terprises. Want an unlimited
field to work in.

Ruler- Neptune.

Mystical, idealistic, Are
devoted and self-sacrifi-
cing. Should avoid being too
secretive. Make good confi-
dants, investigators, execu-
tives in institutions for
the sick, afflicted or crim-
inal. Can develop psychic
gifts to a marked extent.
Have a protective attitude
toward humanity. Good writ-
ers, producers, government
officials,

Apr. 13.

Aries

May 11.
Tau.

June 9.
Gem.

Ruler- Mars,

Eager to express views and
opinions. Want to be out

in front as leaders of the
people. Should avoid bluster-
ing and riding rough shod o-
ver those of divergent beliefs.
Very curious about public re-
actions, Self-promotive and

not always able properly to
evaluate their mission. Work
hard for awhile, then give up.
If the interests are universal
can become great. Succeed as
merchants, public leaders, sur~
geons, publishers.

Ruler- Venus.

Not always sure of their ob-
jectives so should have them
clearly defined and work toward
them. Naturally skeptical. Home
harmony essential; need support,
Must cultivate faith in others.
Attracted to stage-- music or
acting. Have real religious in-
clination, of which they are of-
ten unaware. Apt to be influen-
ced by personalities in their en-
vironment. Should have the cour-
age to pursue and adhere to own
principles, Self-indulgence and
desire for protection makes them
weak and useless.

Ruler- Mercury.

Undecided and vacillating be-
fore 36. Ability for success
but must be allowed to express
their ideals or they will go a-
long with the easiest way. Per-
sonal responsibilities should
not be assumed before they have
found themselves. Naturally ide-
alistic and philanthropic but
are blocked by an eye for expe-
diency. Fine legal minds. Need
people, variety, some travel
and enough cooperation to boost
their self-confidence, Make
good lawyers, journalists, pub-
lic officials, counselors. May
be too procrastinating for own
good. Must stress truth in all
dealings.

## Page 133

education and a cultivated under-
standing.

Among the lesser lights there
is a tendency to work under the
Personality Card-- which invaria-

bly detracts from their power. The

women especially drift into meni-

al work as the easiest way to pro-

vide for their comfort-- but they
usually do their job efficiently
unless too distracted by various
interests outside of it.

Backed by the 10 D (the prece-

ding card), there is often an in-

heritance from the parents or sub-

stantial help from members of the
family. They are excellent "re-
ceivers". The women especially,
but both sexes in general are at~-
tracted to those in the profess-

ional field. They welcome anything
that supports their prestige. Mon-

ey is the great obstacle to their

spiritual growth and therefore the

source of many of their tests.
Through grief or loss or illness,

at some period in their lives-- usu-

ally late-- they are forced to
learn values.

The displacement of the KC

affirms that power is increased by

the search for knowledge. If ear-

ly education has been neglected or

ignored, these people should make
every effort to make up for it by
joining study groups, going to

night school or taking correspond-

ence courses-- no matter at what

age. It is their knowledge and not

their money that will enable them

to take their place among the high

ones.
There is assured success for
them in choosing a career that

deals with health-- nursing, medi-

cine or the healing arts in the
drugless field. Many are attract-
ed to the stage, to education or
to government positions. Among a
few, religion is a fetish.

Plane

=F

oe
ID
=]

2: 2 Ss.

There is a longing for af-
fection and a positive de-
mand for admiration. The emo-
tions are so apt to be affect-
ed by the desire for money
that satisfaction is usually
short-lived and a romance that
starts out enthusiastically

is soon withered if the finan-
cial requirements are not met.
Interested in travel and tran-
sitory contacts. Education is
not usually considered as im-
portant as experience and di-
version until maturity arrives.
Want to live well and if
money is available, want

to do good with it. Self is
very apt to come first, but
generosity is fundamental and
there is usually some important
charity or some individual

who will benefit at their hands.
Family ties are very strong and
they will always see that mem-
bers of their own family are
provided for. Seek association
with those of good financial
background. Are often afflict-
ed with false pride and snob-
bishness. There is a strong de-
sire for a home of their own
and they will make sacrifices
to obtain it.

Are stimulated to effort

by association with suc-
cessful women. They like to
be seen with free spenders
but are unhappy if they can't
keep their end up-- or go them
one better. The placement of
this card in the Saturn Line
indicates the effort required
to amass the amount of money
they want and the disappoint-
ments that arise when obstac-
les present themselves. If
they are temporarily limited,
they often keep out of sight
until they have acquired e-
nough to shine again.

## Page 135

9 NINES 9

INES include all Numbers and
all Planets; 9 is a univer-
sal, all-containing symbol.

As a Birth Card we may empha~
size the Cross of 5 (the Number
of Man) in the venter; we may re-
main within the security of the
two protective (and often limit-
ing) squares at the top and bot-
tom or we may leave the lower tri-
ad behind us, cross the central
path and operate in the higher.

9 is the finisher, for here
we reach the end of the single
digits; it is also the beginning~--
for we at once proceed to another
cycle of 9, which always ends in
9 (18, 27, 36, etc.). It tears
down, sweeps away and terminates~~
but it is never lost because it
always reproduces itself. It des-
troys and it fulfils; it is the
end and the beginning.

Because of its destructive
and expelling force the ancients
allotted it to the planet Mars;
because of its all-ness as oppos~
ed to l-ness, it is called the
Card of Disappointment. It is ac-
tually a Number-- and a Card-- of
complete Fulfilment when we grasp
its meaning and live its law.

The true 9 is dedicated to
service-- anywhere, everywhere,
to anyone or to everyone. It de-
mands the relinquishment of self.
But because of its size and ex-
tension and inclusion-- an over-
all outpouring-- it is the most
emotional influence we have to
deal with. 9's love more than the
rest because they have more "ter-
ritory" to cover-- and they suf-
fer more; they give more than the

rest because they have a greater
store-- and it leaves them more
bereft; they are more idealistic
than the rest because they have
been sent to establish Universal
Love and the Brotherhood of Man--
and they become more disillusioned.

A Card of Disappointment? As=
suredly it is when we chart our
lives by personal loves and per-
sonal desires. A certain portion
of personal love is not denied
-- but it always brings trouble.
9 represents the Great Desire--
but the desire must conform to
the inexorable law or result in
frustration, sorrow and loss.
There is no easy personal pattern
for any of the 9's,

HEARTS have the hardest problem of
them all for they live by
their emotions-~- and Saturn
lays his heavy hand on them;
in God's Plan it is the Ven-
us Card in the Venus Line--
but God's Plan is universal.

CLUBS must seek knowledge for uni-
versal good-- never for
their sole advantage. When
they develop intellectual
snobbishness they are doomed
to failure-- and isolation.

DIAMONDS must acquire-- then "sell
all and give to the poor"

SPADES must "labor in his neigh-
bor's vineyard" before he
may gather his own grapes.

For all there is sacrifice--
and there is no reward without it.
9's do not sign their names or la-
bel their gifts; they are people
of "magnificent obsession". Like
the Number of their Card, they
must lose their identity in order
to find their rightful place.

Sequence e 9 H

Some obstacles to a good
education may be encounter-
ed, but they are not usually
financial. Apt to worry over
things that are transitory
and inconsequential. The ear-
ly trend may be toward sub-
jects in scientific or re~
search lines. Money is wanted
for the power it will bring
or the good it may do. Must
learn to carry through and
not lose interest. Should cul-
tivate a spirit of optimism.
Should watch a tendency to
introversion.

Love and friendship may

cause financial burdens.
Subject to changes in home
and associates. Contacts are
necessary but should be test~
ed before being accepted as
friends. Should never go into
business with friends. Fear
to make investments because
payments might become burden-
some. Can avoid disappoint-
ment by not setting too high
a value on money.

Attracted to professional
women-~ usually older.

Want all associations busi-
nesslike. May have some appo-
sition from a domineering wom-
an-- mother, sister or wife.
Nerves may be affected and
disposition soured by constant
resistance to circumstances,
Must learn to adjust-- but not
be coerced. If willing to work
hard, may confidently expect
adequate payment.

Can benefit by association
with men of intelligence;
should never waste time on the
frivolous and trifling. Are
adapted to success in publish-
ing, journalism-- anything
that reaches far and is widely
known. May take great pride in
some male member of the family

7

e

a

and advance by association
with him. If-a close tie is
formed, this person can be
depended upon.

Disappointment in finan-

ces may affect the health.
Should avoid investments in
real estate, mines and their
products and all things of a
speculative nature. Gain is
made only through strictly
legitimate transactions; no
short cuts or quick turnovers.
If in line for inheritance,
may have trouble in collect-
ing it. Should never borrow
from or lend to women.

Not apt to get full cred-

it for work and should

not harbor that motive. Best
to avoid taking any active
part in groups connected with
labor; no benefit will come
from joining any union. The
chosen occupation should be
well established and along or-
thodox lines. Avoid uncertain-
ties as far as possible. This
is a power Card and the Uran-
us influence always provides
strength for intuition and en-
couragement for its develop-
ment. Those who feel held
"close to the ground" should
work consciously with this
fine force.

Desire for wisdom increas~

es with the years. If trav-
el is desired and possible, a
congenial mental companion
should be sought. Latent fears
can be overcome by study of
metaphysics. Study with others
for growth and inspiration. Af-
ter 50 there is an inclination
to become "joiners", These peo-
ple will be happier if not ob-
liged to live alone but emo-

tional involvement is not good.

## Page 139

NINE OF CLUBS

Clubs ~ Knowledge
gc ~ Obstacles to Mental Con-
trol
9 in C - Knowledge Universally
Applied

The Saturn Card in the Venus L,
Displaces the Q H in the Nat. Sp.

This is an excellent example
of the workings of the Law of 9.
As in the case of the 9 H the po~
sition is Saturn, indicating a
struggle in relation to any men-
tal (Clubs) development. The dif-
ficulty could be due to finances
but since we are in the Venus
Line and the Displacement Card
is the Q H, it is much more apt
to be due to the native's procli-
vity for wasting time and emotion-
al energy on frivolity and self-
indulgence. (The Q H can be a dis-
tracting and demoralizing influ-
ence). We find the "answer" as
well as safe guidance when we
note the True Place. Here the 9 C
is the Mercury Card in the Jupiter
Line-- fortified by the proximity
of the 10 C, Expansion (Jup.) for
mental (Clubs) development; forget
the venusian (Line) satisfactions
and hew to the line of duty (Sat-
urn) if you would eliminate the
disappointments (9) that are sure
to follow the negative operation
of your Birth Card. God's Plan
for you is ruled by Mercury and
Jup; by following it you will
turn all loss (9) into fulfilment
(9).

As a rule, these people have
warm and friendly personalities
and a keen sense of obligation.
They keep promises and pay debts,
Note that the True Place of the 9
C is displaced by the 6 D, estab-
lishing still another connection
with the Birth Card. All 6's are

working with karmic law-- and
know it-- so there is no desire
to escape responsibility

Without getting too far out
of line as far as duty is con-
cerned, the 9 C is an adventur-
er's card. They like to gamble
and are always willing to take
a chance for the satisfaction of
curiosity or interest. When the
adventurous spirit extends to the
field of knowledge, they often be-
come extremists-- but at least
they are seeking and they are ca~
pable of making some discovery
that is of wide benefit.

When not influenced by the
wrong kind of women, association
with one of kindliness and human-
itarian qualities increases their
own. They worry too much and are
too dependent upon approval and
sympathy. Many of the early dif-
ficulties and gropings disappear
in middle life-- or as soon as
they are ready to settle down and
lay aside the objectives that are
strictly personal and emotional.

The women especially must
watch the tendency to flirtatious-
ness and triviality. The satisfac-
tion (if any) is always transito-
ry and the chances for a dependa-
ble and harmonious association
may be spoiled.

Any close association formed
with 6 D or QH birthdates is an
indication that there is a karmic
element in the experience gained.
All 9's have come to pay off old
obligations NOW and in the case
of the 9 C these people (6 D and
Q H) constitute some of the agents
or "collectors". The less they
express through the personality,
the surer their fulfilment.

2D

-137-

If a commercial line is
chosen, can deal success-
fully with foreigners and for-
eign countries, Strongly at-
tracted to travel-- but it may
be mental rather than actual.
Are intuitive and inspiration-
al and can develop extra~sen-
sory perception if they work
at it. In this regard are al-
ways safer in very small se-
lected groups or with one de-
veloped person. Should avoid
public seances. Protection
must always be asked for when
engaging in this work and it
should be left alone until due
preparation has been made.

lenge for the 9

MENTAL AND EMOTIONAL WEAKNESS

ites 2 Cc

Jan. 31.
Aquar.

Feb. 29.
Pisc.

Ruler- Uranus.

If home life provides a

good anchorage, work goes
well. Interested in labor and
politics-- but not in holding
any office. Best success in
mental lines-- newspapers, in-
terviews, personnel managers,
etc. Dramatic in manner. Can
often succeed in the theatre;
showmanship carries them far.
Gift for writing-- seriously.
Unorthodox; defy established
customs.

Ruler- Neptune.

A rare birthdate. Should
cultivate balance and

guard against erraticism. Are
very intuitive-- on the psy-
chic side; temperamental. May
become soft and lazy. Should
choose work that allows them
to serve unless there is some
outstanding talent. Make fine
dancers if willing to work on
technique. Lean to poetry or
poetic prose in writing. Must
avoid psychic experiments and
be sure of their ground.

Mar. 27.
Aries,

Apr. 25,

Tau.

May 23.
Gem.

June 21,
Gem.

Ruler- Mars.

Very self-determined; in-
clined to egotism. Make
friends easily but are always
looking out for #1. Good-
natured but have quick tem-
pers. Good starters, Must a-
void becoming mercenary. Are
successful as lawyers (pros-
ecutors), politicians, sci-
entists. Many are universally
minded, progressive and mil-
itant for reforms.

Ruler~ Venus.

Creative and inventive.

Work best if there is a
heart-interest. Want to live
well and have security for
the whole family; often have
to create it themselves and
not depend upon the mate.
May write but are best adapt-
ed for artistic work-- paint-
ing, singing, dramatics, mod-
eling, composing. Excellent
designers and decorators.
Ruler- Mercury.

Dissatisfied with results,
Impatient, changeable.

Give up too easily. Always
have a mental approach. Good
draughtsmen, architects, cri-
tics, journalists. Opinionat-
ed. Skilful with hands and
with words. Speakers, report-
ers, translators. Good lin-
guists. Attracted to theatre,
radio, electricity. Always
make themselves heard and
felt in any crowd.

Ruler- Mercury.

Less “touch and go" than

the other Gem. birthdate;
more public-spirited. If they
remain impersonal, can make
considerable money. Want a
home but not always happily
married. Good guides or trav-
el agents, canvassers, stew-
ards, demonstrators, etc.
Good entertainers, hosts and
companions. More optimistic
than many 9 C but may have
long fits of depression.

NINE _OF DIAMONDS

Diamonds - Values

gD - Dissatisfaction in
Money
9 in D ~- Generosity-- or Sel-
fishness

The Mars Card in the Uranus Line
Displaces the Q D in the Nat. Sp.

There seems to be no middle
ground for these people; they are
either philanthropic, generous and
protective toward others or live
for themselves alone, unable to
acquire the money they want and
dissatisfied with life. For all
9's, there is no escaping obsta-
cles and disappointment if they
are selfish. The True Place is
the Neptune Card in the Saturn
Line-- which is but another way
of saying that duty, responsibil-
ity and full payment constitute
the goal in life and should be
idealized and sought eagerly. When
it is, it is attained happily.

There are no weaklings in the
birthdates of this Card-- but in
early life or in the case of some
strong attachment, there is a ten-
dency to be dominated. When this
occurs, once the tie is broken,
they may become domineering them-
selves-~ to "get even''. There is
usually a goodly amount of self-
insistence and aggressiveness.
They want to think and act for
themselves-- and should-- but
fear they may not be able to un-
less they demand it.

There is a close tie between
the 9 D and the Q D-- a tie that
surpasses the displacement influ-
ence. Those belonging to these
dates have some karmic debt to
work out-- and the association
is not always an agreeable one.
In the case of a woman, there is
a "double dose" to be reckoned

with and great care should be ta-
ken in handling these associa-
tions.

For the most part, these peo-
ple are slated for success. They
are inclined to materiality-- and
may be mercenary, but the natural
tendency is toward generosity,
even though they never forget to
protect themselves.

If they are to avoid disap-
pointment, they must clearly de-
fine their values-- and they
should be helped to this end very
early in life. "As the twig is
bent" is very significant in their
case and colors their entire life.
Those whose inclinations are on
the spiritual level and have ac-
quired a working philosophy have
few obstacles to overcome. Con~
sciously or unconsciously they
follow the Law of 9 and GIVE of
themselves, their efforts and
their goods. With any 9, a cer-
tain degree of "cosmic urge" is
a requirement. Those who deny it
only defeat themselves.

The women have more to over-
come than the men for they are al-
ways struggling with their person-
ality-- and that QD is difficult.
The men are apt to marry women
who cause them worry, cost them
money or fail to give satisfac~
tion.

Both sexes are apt to over~
estimate their ability. Both are
interested in things that move
too fast and are therefore sub~
ject to accidents.

They often choose~- and are
well adapted for-- welfare work,
Red Cross, Salvation Army, YMCA,
or some allied branch of public
service. The less they concentrate
on their own security, the better.

~141-
2 e 9 D

FAITH IN THE GOLDEN CALF

Birthdates Ruled by the 9 D

Jan. 18, Ruler-- Saturn

Cap.

Feb.

16.

Aquar.

Mar.
Pisc.

14.

Scholarly, thorough, in-
dustrious. Ambitious and
studious. Approach everything
from a mental angle. Orthodox
and cautious; take no chances,
For Capricorn-- quite univer-
sally minded. No imagination.
Can write if along solid and
serious lines. Want to cover
a large field-~ big business,
big audiences, a big "place".
Successful in manufacturing
and merchandising.

Ruler~ Uranus

These people are critical

and controversial. Like

to argue and often take the
opposite side-- not from con~
viction but because they en-
joy it. Interested in people
and the rights of the under-
dog. More biased than bal-
anced; go "all out" for any
cause they espouse. Imagina-
tion, enthusiasm and emotion-
alism carries many into the
theatre-- often to marked suc-
cess. Can also succeed as cor-
respondents, columnists or
government officials.

Ruler- Neptune.

Very talented in art or
music (also dancing) or

very scientific, capable of
making a valuable contribu-
tion to general knowledge and
progress. Idealistic and hu-
manitarian, In the less gift-
ed and intellectual there is
a tendency to drift, Benefit-
ted by interests at a dist-
ance. Make good agents, man-
agers of transportation, hos-
pital or prison employees,
secret service investigators.
May gain through perfumes, oil,
narcotics or fishing.

Apr. 12. Ruler- Mars

Aries

May 10.
Tau.

June 8.
Gem.

July 6.
Can.

Promoters, politicians,
members of armed forces,
orators and propagandists.
May also succeed in publish-
ing. The majority are not
attracted to merchandising.
Always self-promotive-- often
too aggressive and egotistic.
Good talkers, good salesmen,
and like a good fight. Feel
very sure of themselves,
Ruler- Venus

Good leaders, directors,

and initiators. Like to

be associated with groups

and clubs but want some of-
ficial position near the

top. Work well with others

if allowed to keep their in-
dependence. Honest and reli-
able; affectionate and pro-
tective. Attracted to intel-
ligent women. Can commercial-
ize products for general use.
Good cooks and gardeners.
Ruler- Mercury.

Mental and inquiring. Are
highly nervous-- which af-
fects the health. Usually
want more power, authority
and money than they can han-
dle or acquire. Apt to devel-
op chronic conditions due to
negative states of mind and
a tendency to hypochrondria,.
Good traders, writers, talk-
ers, extemporaneous speakers.
Illnesses and obstacles of-
ten come unexpectedly; sur-
prising changes. Should be
careful of lungs.

Ruler~ The Moon

Patriots and sticklers for
principle. Sincere devo-
tees of worthy causes, Objec~
tives often delayed until la-
ter years. Good government
leaders and officials. When
merchandising is chosen, usu-
ally deal in small articles,
home products, foods. Not an
easy birthdate; life full of
effort and hard work.
