Merc.
24H

2B
FA

KD

-143-

equence for the 9 S

Sudden and transitory ev-
ents characterize the ear-

ly years. Likely to marry
young-~ after several love
affairs. Need contacts and
companionship but want intel-
ligence and a desire for know-
ledge in associations. Make
strong attachments but can
let go of them without undue
pain when they prove unsatis~
factory. Easily attracted to
the opposite sex-- not always
wisely. Not outstanding gen-
eral students but eagerly pur-
sue knowledge that is connect-
ed with their main interest.
Men friends important and
influential; friendships
formed with those older are
permanent unless the tie be-
comes too emotional and some
break is caused through jeal-
ousy. Can be helpful and val-
uable but should not be al-
lowed to impose domination.
The father or older brother
may exert too strong an in-
fluence and become restrict-
ive. The women may marry ol-
der men-- protective but
paternal-~ and may chafe un-
der the relationship.
Occupation is involved

with monied people or en-~
tails handling considerable
sums. If a connection can be
formed with those of means

or who are dealing in min-
erals, many of the business
difficulties of the 9 S will
be mitigated. If these asso-
ciations are formed, there is
always an element of uncer-
tainty in them. Liable to
breaks and displacements.
The greatest benefits come

if changes are avoided and

a chosen course adhered to.
Security lies in established
conditions which provide a

ak
alr

E

a
n

steady, ample income rather
than affluence. Work flour~
ishes more freely when based
on friendly relations, Work
and application should be
steady but not allowed to
produce a rut.

Peace of mind contributes

to good health; nerves

and a spirit of discontent
are bound to interfere with
it. These people can become
mental healers and are them-
selves responsive to mental
therapy. When well balanced,
have a soothing and curative
effect on the mentally dis-
turbed. May have a skeptical
attitude of mind-- which
should be overcome; inwardly
know better than to doubt.
Fear of financial inse-
curity interferes with
their work and the "direct
contact" they are well able
to establish. Should never
have to worry about money
(and need not) unless they
are deliberately wasteful.
Work with more contentment
and freedom if associated
with some one who will at-
tend to the details (and ex-
penditures). Can make money
from real estate and should
own their own homes.

Have original and pecu-

liar ideas-- sometimes
considered erratic. High id-
eals, but have difficulty in
realizing them. This is a neo~
phyte's card; debts must be
paid before any further prog-
ress can be made-- and there
is a great desire for prog-
ress along spiritual lines,
Worry and material concern
get in the way' once these
are overcome, "illunination"
is assured. Travel is apt to
be disappointing. Emotional
ties become less important
in the later years.

## Page 149

10 TENS 10

ULLY ACCOMPLISHED" or "ALL

COMPLETE" is the translation
of the Greek word Panteleia-~ the
Decad or the Number Ten.

TENS are called "Success"
Cards-- a term that seems far too
weak to apply to such a powerful
symbol. To the Pythagoreans 10
represented Deity, Heaven, Eter-
nity and the Sun*. To ourselves
10 is Man (1) and "God Ahead"(0).
-- a heaven to reach for, though
we may not grasp it.

9, with all the numbers be-
hind it, is the completed cycle
of man's experience; 10 begins
the new cycle, on a higher spiral,
the cycle of man's Aspiration,

On the tree of Life there are
10 Spheres or "10 Emanations of
the Divine Sephiroth" and Malkuth,
the Kingdom is the 10th-- our own
world; in the Pattern on the Tres~-
tleboard there are 10 Statements;
our laws of conduct were given in
10 Commandments and the Decimal
system is used all over the world.
Unattainable as it may appear and
"mighty'"' as it surely is, 10 is
ur number to use and to "succeed"
with. If 10 is your Birth Card
you have the tools with which to
“fully accomplish".

In the Mundane Spread we have
placed one of the 10's in the ex-
act center (it would be diamonds!);
another stands behind it; a third
is the center of the Mercury Line
and the fourth leads the Sun or
"Crown" Line. In any position in
which the card is held, we find
the triangle-- symbol of perfect-

* W. Wynn Westcott, "Numbers",

ion in expression. Here is success
on all sides, as man stands in
the center-- two patterns of 5
(the number of man), carrying

the protection of the pentagram.
Every 10 should consciously live
in the realization that he is

Man twice over-- Man as himself
and Man in the image of God. So
are we all-- but 10 is the only
card that has that 0 ever beside
it. No forward step can be taken
without meeting it-- face to face.

Since What Constitutes Suc-
cess is a purely individual ques-
tion, we find every variety of
expression in these 10's-- a few
of the very great, more of the
very successful and the vast ma-
jority who are utterly oblivious
to the power in the equipment
they have brought to earth as
their kit of tools. None of them
can be wholly devoid of elements
of greatness but many can and do
live as though the purpose
of life were to amass, attain and
control. But not even the atheist
escapes his divine origin,

HEARTS attain their success and
overcome their obstacles
through the power of Love.

CLUBS find their success in the
mental field and secure
it by sharing their know-
ledge.

DIAMONDS succeed as Masters of Mat-
ter. Their dominion is over
“all created things".

SPADES success depends upon the
degree of maturity they
have reached. For them,

10 is their intiation into
a higher Grade,

## Page 151

-147-

Planetary Sequence for the 10 H

Merc.
10D

AH

Money transactions are
disposed of easily and
quickly. There are ample funds
in early life and always the
possibility of inheritance,
The majority are brought up in
pleasant surroundings, with
good opportunity for educa~
tion and culture. The women
may marry with money in mind
but will make every effort to
contribute to the success of
their husbands.

Interested in large groups

-- educational or reli-~

gious. The less serious mem-
bers of these dates spend much
time entertaining and making a
success of running their homes.
They take pride in good organ-
ization and efficiency and en-
joy impressing others with the
domestic greased wheels, They
prefer to surround themselves
with people of high intelli-
gence and interesting ideas;
if they are "important" as
well, they are so much the
more welcome.

Want to stand well and be
popular-- especially with

the opposite sex. May be too
much influenced by the finan-
cial standing of their friends.
Are good hosts and good mixers,
never at their best when alone.
There is always a sense of
leadership and initiative and
they want their ideas and deci-
sions unquestioned. They think
they know best~-- and they of-
ten do-- but if their poli-
cies are voted down, they will
gracefully step aside rather
than take second place,

There is always ambition

and pride of place. Their

good reputation must be pres~-
erved at all costs and faults,
lacks and family skeletons are
carefully concealed, They are

oF
Io
a

fine custodians of secrets--
others' as well as their own.
If there is a temporary finan-
cial shortage, the world sel-
dom hears of it; they manage
to cover it up until they are
again on their money feet--
having made great sacrifices
to maintain "business as us-
ual",

If there has been a marri-

age (or any other partner-
ship) contracted for the sake
of money, trouble catches up
with them in some form or oth-
er, Their life may be inter-
fered with by some sick or nag~
ging female member of the fam-
ily or by a dependent who may
make unreasonable demands.

The women may become success~
ful physicians or important
nurses or executives in a doc-
tor's office, They do not lack
sympathy but want to be fully
paid for their services.

Work is subject to change

and variety and there is
often considerable travel in
connection with it. An occu~
pation is sought where the hu-
man element is involved-- for
contacts are desirable and
successful. Dealings in real
estate are not recommended,
nor are speculative invest-
ments. They believe in prog-
ress and are open to new ideas
-- which will be revamped and
stamped with their own orig-
inality. In groups they will
assume the leadership. If de-
nied or thwarted in love they
will turn to metaphysics.
Their beliefs are definite
but they are not always

sure of their origin-- or
their worth. If they change
them, it remains their secret.
Travel is not satisfactory in
later life. They should pro-
tect themselves in ample time
against the threat of loneliness.

## Page 153

-149-

TEN_OF CLUBS

Clubs - Knowledge

10 C - Mental Illumination

10 in C - The Will to Good plus
the Science of Mind

The Mercury Card in the Crown L.
Displaces the J S in the Nat. Sp.

As has been previously stated,
the Crown or "Sun" Cards have the
privilege of choosing their posi-
tion-- but do not depart from the
inherent qualities of suit or num-
ber.

10 C, being the first card in
its line, is under the rulership
of Mercury and is therefore condi-
tioned by all that planet stands
for-- mental processes, approaches
and reactions; ideas and communi-
cations; education and mind-train-
ing. Being Clubs, it symbolizes
knowledge-- its acquisition and
dissemination. Regardless of the
position under which it may "choose"
to operate-~ together with an addi-
tional planetary influence-- its
basic "ingredients" remain.

The displacement of the JS
suggests the danger of fixation.
The firmmess in the J S and adhe~
rence to principle are well worthy
of emulation, but 10 C can go as~
tray through stubborness.

Their greatest success inva-
triably lies in the mental field.
If their knowledge is applied from
high motives, their needs are sup-
plied from the "Limitless Sub-
stance"; there is seldom any real
lack of supply although they of-
ten fear limitation. They are look-
ing toward the 8 D in their own
Line and they should have no trou~
ble in establishing a right sense
of values. Again looking forward,
the K S gives power through wisdom.

The teachers and initiates
of these dates may "choose" the
8 D as their Jupiter Card and can
make it effective in that posi-
tion if they are reaching out for
attainment in terms of the soul.

If they choose to work with
a wider pattern, the A C becomes
the Mercury Card and the arrange-
ment reads as follows:

KS 8D 10¢
AS 3D 5€ 10S QC AC 3H

In this case, however, they
may complicate the emotional life
by their close proximity to the
uncertain 3 H. In the educational
field there would be no problems.

There is always the power to
make money-- but the effort is
sometimes lacking. The gift of
choice may become a source of con-
fusion for they can't always tell
just where they are or should be
operating. They want to be pro-
ductive and successful but if they
have not reached the stage in
their development where they can
depend upon intuitional guidance;
they sometimes waste many valuable
years in experimentation before
they find the right vocation.
"Make your calling and election
sure" said St. Paul-- and he
must have been talking directly
to the 10 Cc.

The True Place is the Venus
Card in the Jupiter Line. The gift
of Knowledge is not the only star
in their crown; in the Plan, Love
shines beside it with equal bril-
liance-- love of their work and
love for those with whom they have
come to share their knowledge.
Those who are working in that con-
sciousness are Jupiter's own heirs.

## Page 155

-151-

Birthdates Ruled by the 10 C

Jan. 30.
Aquar.

Feb. 28,
Pisc.

Mar. 26.
Aries.

Ruler- Uranus.

Very ambitious people

and fully equipped for
leadership. Can excel in
any line they choose and
should not be hampered by
equal partnerships or asso-
ciates from whom they must
take orders, Always willing
to work hard and always work
for improvement. Art or sci-
ence are the best fields--
with government offices a
close second, Exceptional
qualities and unusual pop-
ularity may elevate them

to high government positions.
Ruler- Neptune

Restless and changeable

and may suffer from peo-

ple who are changeable them-
selves-- and unreliable. May
become famous in music, dra-~
ma or art, but often lack ap-
plication and persistence.
Subject to accidents through
carelessness or day-dreaming.
Like travel and a variety of
interests but should guard
against a tendency to lazi-
ness. Should seek advice in
making investments.

Ruler- Mars.

Work well by fits and
starts. Too apt to lose
interest and abandon a pro-
ject that gives promise of
success through persistence.
Like to lay out a progress~
ive plan and leave it to oth-
ers to execute. Want to make
money quickly; not so good
for the long pull. Work well
with women as employees, not
as partners. Good promoters.
Good dealers or executives
in artistic lines but are
seldom gifted as artists or
performers. Cultivation of
an attractive personality
goes far toward success,

Apr. 24.
Tau.

May 22.
Tay. or
Gem.

June 20.
Gem.

Ruler~ Venus.

Responsible and protect-

ive. May become leaders
through willingness to res~
pond to the demands made up~
on them. Must be kings in
their own homes. Like to be
entertained and waited upon.
Attracted to the stage-- as
actors. If business is cho-
sen, want it big. Fair and
honest in all dealings, Emo-
tional and warm-hearted. Can
write fluently and dramati-
cally. If in a government po-
sition, more fatherly than
dictatorial.

Rulers- Venus or Mercury.
Those who still carry the
stamp of Taurus are in-
clined to acting, composing
and playwriting and can eas-
ily commercialize their tal-
ents. The Gemini-born are
more mental than emotional

or dramatic. These may succeed
in the educational field, as
eritics or satirical writers,
essayists, etc. All are affec-
ted by home conditions; in-
harmony interferes with abil-
ity to concentrate-- and con-
sequent success. Deep inter-
est (Tau.) or curiosity (Gem.)
in metaphysics.

Ruler- Mercury.

Writers, lecturers, poli-
ticians. Should be before
the public. Clever and versa-
tile. Willing to give service
if interested in the "cause".
Like to deal with people and
changing conditions. Always
curious about what makes peo-
ple (or things) "tick". Have
ups and downs in finances,
Often undertake more than
they can carry through. Want
business that is quick-mov-
ing, bringing quick returns.
Liable to become over-extend-
ed. Not as sure of themselves
as the Geminis of May 22nd.

## Page 157

TEN OF DIAMONDS

Diamonds ~ Values
- A Master of Matter

40D
10 in D - A Leader in Material
Control

The Jupiter Card in the Jupiter L.
Displaces the Q C in the Nat. Sp.

This is the most important of
the money cards for it is in the
exact center of the Mundane Spread.
Man chose to make money the pivot~
al point around which all else
should swing and selected the most
powerful of the money cards to
guarantee "success". 10 D is one
of the Master Cards.

In the Divine Plan Receptivity
and Intelligence is the focal
point-- and while these qualities
are relegated to second place in
the eyes of the world, the aware
ones may "borrow" them by virtue
of displacement.

The majority of these natives
are money conscious but there are
many who are, instead, yalue con-
scious-~ a very different matter.
They translate their "full accom-
plishment" into cosmic terms.

In general, there is a lack
of true spirituality. The type of
religion they profess is tradition-
al and orthodox; the goal they
prize is Acquisition. They are in
great danger of becoming mercenary.

This is a better card for a
man than a woman; the men can ay~
oid the Q D and its unfortunate
sequence. For both sexes, there is
usually the promise of inheritance.
They can always succeed and are al-
ways protected where money is in-
volved. They may get down to the
last dollar, threatened with loss

of business or property-- and
then, by clever manipulation or
last-minute help, turn the threat-
ened failure to success.

If a man, will benefit by asso-
ciation with a successful woman;
if a woman, is likely to be in
business for herself or in a key
position of management. They all
like to associate with people who
have something to offer-~ if not
actual money, then position or so-
cial standing or family back-
ground. They are not necessarily
snobs but they want to stand well
in the eyes of the world and they
want their surroundings to give
evidence of prosperity.

Commercializing their abili-
ties comes easily. If they engage
in business, they never fear size
or extent; they know they can han-
dle it-- and make it pay.

The True Place is the Mercury
Card in the Uranus Line. There are
few who lack keen brains and sharp
wits and while their education is
sought primarily along business
lines, they have great respect for
knowledge and want to acquire en-
ough of it to be able to take
their place in any company.

There are many philanthropists
and benefactors in these birth-
dates, many with a strong sense
of universal obligation and a de-
sire to put their money to construc-
tive use. They are invariably gen-
erous with any surplus-- and some
there are who will deprive them-
selves to help the less fortunate.
Great buildings, enterprises and
monuments have been established
in their name and many good deeds
live after them. They are tested
by their sense of values.

Challenge for the 10 D
EXPEDIENCY IN ASSOCIATIONS
b D

17. Ruler- Saturn.

Very patriotic. Excellent
government officials-- am-
bassadors, representatives,
diplomats. Interested in so-
ciological questions, state
or federal laws, government
procedure. If in business,
usually for themselves. Self-
confident in the business
world-- not in their emotion-
al lives; changeable in feel-
ings. Want to be associated
with things that are well es-
tablished; no gamblers. Can
succeed in oil, mining and
manufacturing.

Ruler- Uranus

Famous actors, writers

and educators are found

in this birthdate. Always
have a large following; their
works have a wide distribu-
tion. Personal lives disturb-
ed by doubt and unrest. Make
good salespeople, attorneys
and realtors. Interested in
labor problems. Want spirit-
ual security but do not know
how to cultivate it. Should
make a determined study of
metaphysics,

Ruler- Neptune

Less self-confident than

the other 10 D. Full of
fears and worries. Build
their world around their own
small circle. Give willing
service-- but always person-
al. Can succeed in transpor-
tation; like travel but sel-
dom satisfied with journeys.
Good musicians; may be good
dancers. Dutiful and devoted
nurses. Should serve in broad
fields-- impersonally. Lives
often narrow and unproductive,

15.

13.

Apr. 11.

Aries.

May 9.
Tau.

June 7.
Gen.

July 5.
Can.

Ruler- Mars

Square-dealing; honest,
Nervous and emotional.
Ambitious; dominated by a
desire to stand well. Will-
ing to serve, but want full
payment. Need plenty of ac-
tion to be happy. Not con-
tent with small or inactive
business. Can succeed at law
but should not become judges;
too emotional and biased.
Swayed by personal opinions
and fixed ideas. Very moral,
Should avoid intolerance.
Ruler- Venus.

Want harmony at home and
among friends. Want to

stand well and put up a good
front. Combine business with
social activities, Ruled by
emotions and ambition. Apply
their efforts to accumulation.
Make good doctors; have good
“bedside manners". Can succeed
in real estate, home furnish-
ings, food. Not always as uni-
versally-minded as their birth-
day number requires. Climbers.
Ruler- Mercury

Want quick turnovers. Will
work only if interested.

Can lecture, teach-- and make
money at it. Can overcome the
tendency to superficiality by
cultivating the mind. Have a
variety of skills. Give the
impression of instability but
are often serious-- even de~
pressed. Uncertain of right
place; will make many experi-
ments before settling down.
Can sell if they have faith
in the product, A mental occu-
pation best for success.
Ruler~ The Moon.

Seek important and success-
ful people as "background".
Self-indulgent. Dislike too
much work or effort. Expect
help from others. Can be pub-
lic-spirited and philanthrop-
ic. Writers, philosophers,

TEN SPADES
Spades - Labor; The Path to Wisdom. ambition to seek a pattern of
10s ~ Success in Work and Dev- greater development. For the men
elopment. of all cards up to the Court
10 in S - Glorification of Labor. group, there are three planes of

The Jupiter Card in the Mercury L.
Displaces the 4 H in the Nat. Sp.

For these people home and bus-
iness are closely associated-- and
the one may seriously interfere
with the other. They are often
found conducting their business at
home, hampered by constant inter-
ruptions and lack of application.

While 10's are Success Cards,
the natives are not always success~
ful people-- even though they are
invariably protected up to a cer-
tain point. This is especially
true of the 10 S, for his achieve-
ment depends entirely upon the de-
gree of maturity he has reached.
Until 36, he is usually operating
(in the case of the men) under the
JS; thereafter he may choose the
King-- if he has the spiritual

Sept. 1. Ruler- Mercury

operation-~ the Birth Card, the
mental card (J) and the rulership
card (K). For the women there

are but two-- the Birth Card and
the Personality (Q); if the Q is
the Birth Card there is, of course,
no alternate.

The position of the 10 S is
similar to a Mercury-Jupiter con-
junction-- a combination of good
mind and good judgment. We note
that it is crowned by the 8 D
so these qualities may be espec~
ially operative in the realm of
finance. That this is not always
the case is due to the fact that
we are not always aware of our
"crowns" so fail to wear them.

In the majority of cases these
people are successful in commer-
cial lines. They are more stimula-
ted when the turnover is speedy--
mail order, telephone, messages.


## Page 161

<157=

Development, awareness-- and
especially the urge to seek the
wisdom they have come to acquire
-- are often delayed until middle
life. Operating under the J can
and often does result in shift~
lessness and irresponsibility; if
that persists, the birthright is
lost and the 10 S goes down to a
defeat that is all the more igno-~
minious because of his high call-
ing.

Home life may be neglected for
business, or vice versa. The dis-
placement of the 4 H causes love
and its security to be an import-
ant factor. Unnecessary sacrifices
are made in its name and a result-
ant self-undoing defeats the main
objectives.

The AS (the Mars force) -~ is
the Master Card for these 10 S,
When the desire for wisdom is
paramount, they may become Kings
in their own right and assume
full command over their material
affairs. For the women there is
&@ greater problem; they may be
weakened by negative operation
under the Queen and may become
household servants or drudges.

One is never sure of just
what course these natives will
take-- nor are they always sure
themselves. Their potential is
great; their performance often
below the level of mediocrity.
Working toward the K S -- the high-
est of the initiates-- may seem
too distant a goal to strive for.

IHOOOGOE

Planetary Sequence e 10 S

Willing to change their

minds if convinced of rea-
sonableness. They do not have
to work as hard for spiritual
unfoldment as the 10 D and
will begin earlier in life.
Make frequent changes because
of dissatisfaction and a de-
sire for improvement. A new
viewpoint often brings gain
and they try to keep an open
mind for friendly advice. The
amount of progress in school
depends largely upon the tea-~
cher; they will work hard

for those they like; they will
make a change if the personal-
ity is uncongenial.
Emotionally disturbed by

3D conflicts in the home--

often caused by financial lim-
itation. This helps to give
undue emphasis to money and
friends may be chosen from ul-
terior motives. They expect

to work and prefer not to be
dependent, but the uncertain-
ty about what work to choose
for the speediest returns of-
ten lands them in a job that
is beneath their capabilities
-- and there they may stay
for a long time, fearing to
risk a better one.
This card is the test of
AS their seeking. If they
are aware of the need for de~
velopment, they could not have
a stronger influence to set
them on the path; if they are
indifferent or ignorant they
become loafers or "time" work-
ers-- just enough to get by.
In many cases there is a se-
cret marriage or elopment;
secrecy in some form is com-
mon to all of them, From a
more constructive angle, this
makes them useful in secret
service work and many reach
the top in the Intelligence
Department,

## Page 163

11 JACKS 11

ACKS represent Mentality. Are

willing to learn by experience

and may become a power through
training the mind. On the other
hand, they may become tramps and
wanderers.

They make their living through
their individual efforts-- writing,
composing, selling their ideas,
promoting, advertising or the type
of journalism that involves for-
eign countries. They are always in
search of experience or adventure.
They represent Youth-- and, from
one angle, the neuter gender.

There are many superstitions
connected with the Number 11- the
correspondence with the llth Card
of the Little Book. By some it was
called the Number of Evil because
it transcended the number of the
commandments and did not attain
12- the number of "Grace and Per-
fection". History and experience
refute the stigma and we have come
to regard 1l-- as a Number-- one
of the most priceless gifts of the
gods. It is man(1) beside God
(10), eager to blaze the trail of
return to Kother, the Crown.

1l is the direct recipient of
inspiration from the One Source--
the preacher, messenger and Light-
bearer from On High. 11 is the
mumber of the Path on the Tree of
Life that is assigned to Aleph,
the first Tarot Card, the Magi-
cian, in the direct line from
Kether to Chokmah cr Will to Wis-
dom. It is the "Spirit" of Air--
the "Divine Breath", It was not
by accident that Jacks--1l-- were
assigned as "ushers" of the Court
Cards-- the first inheritors of

the crown.

Jacks carry a great respon-
sibility and because they are the
symbol of two 1's (11), the dis-
posal of their lives rests entire-
ly on their own decision. They
represent the mental attitudes of
the Birth Cards of their individ-
ual suits-- and if we have gone
any distance at all in the pro-
cess of development, we know that
our mental attitudes are wholly
within our own control. We may
rule them and earn our "crowns" or
we may consign them to every wind
that blows "where it listeth" and
bask or struggle in a state of im-
maturity as long as we live.

Jacks are the "divine andro-
gynes"~- the Christ-nature toward
which we are evolving-- or the
vacillating neuters who are nei-
ther one thing nor the other, in-
capable of decision or direction.
In all of them, however, there is
a certain fixity and stubborness;
when it is the result of maturity
and applies to principle, it is
a quality to be praised-- but too
often it is the expression of in-
grained triviality, irresponsib-
ility and shiftlessness, the youth
who must have his own way because
he knows no better.

HEARTS win their crown through
sacrifice for love.
CLUBS through the spoken WORD.
DIAMONDS through good guardian-
ship of their birthright.
SPADES because they have chosen
the path of initiation.

All are our elder brothers.
All are sons of the King.

©
E
wn

2H

-161-
ice the J H

Early education may be
interrupted or partially
sacrificed for the sake of
some member of the family.
When this is the case they
will accept it cheerfully and
pursue their studies on the
"catch as catch can" princi-
ple. They are mentally inclin-
ed and learn easily from what
they see, hear and read, Mere
attendance at school seems to
them of little importance.
They surmount their obstacles
or disregard them.

Emotions are easily dis-
turbed and frequently as-
sailed. Trials and disappoint-
ments in the home life are a
big factor in this difficult
path. There is usually a lack
of understanding and coopera-
tion, The life may be inter-
fered with by ill health of
some member of the family.
Marriage is not apt to be sat-
isfactory emotionally or some
unforeseen problem in connec-
tion with the marriage part-
ner may have to be met, The

J H people are continually
tested in their love life,
Want companionship and

work better in association
with others. Like to mingle
with those who are well infor-
ed and learn quickly from them.
Friendships are important; if
they are broken, the suffering
is keen. That is where their
natural optimism does not serve
them well; they are slow to re-
cover from severed ties. Are
very responsive to friendliness
in work-associations; usually
well served by employees.

Success comes mainly thro
their own efforts but may
be helped by a friendly person
who is mentally congenial.
Should keep the management of

+
E
a

their affairs in their own
hands and not doubt their
ability to handle them, Have
a certain amount of self-
confidence but are fearful
of expansion and experiments.
May become more venturesome
as they grow older.

May reach a position of
leadership through their

own merit or efforts, but do
not seek publicity or the
spotlight because of it. Mod-
est and unassuming; seldom
ambitious for fame or place.
May have a hard-headed fath-
er who may try to force their
career into an uncongenial
channel-- notably medicine.
The majority are not well ad-
apted for drugs or surgery
but often make good magnetic
healers and metaphysicians.

A further emphasis on

the Christ Principle.

Succeed best in some humani-
tarian pursuit and are usual-
ly attracted to it. Dislike
changes and may get into a
rut by refusing to make them.
Should not submit to uproot-
ing, however; can work more
smoothly and successfully if
they become firmly establish-
ed in one place. If working
for others, very loyal to
the job and the employer. U-
sually popular with co-work-
ers.

The later years are more
successful and more con-
fortable than youth or middle
age. Apt to come into their
own toward the end of life.
May become directly in touch
with the higher forces-- of-
ten clairaudiently. Will en-
joy travel and lecturing or
teaching. May have great
success as teacher or leader
in some religious movement
or spiritual work. Mental
awareness increases with the
years.

## Page 167

JACK OF CLUBS

Clubs - Intelligence
ic - THE WORD-- Spoken
il_in ¢ ~- Mental Inspiration

The Venus Card in the Uranus L.
Displaces the J D in the Nat. Sp.

This is a Card of Memory.

As a rule, those people have
this gift in an extraordinary de-
gree. Such a wealth of knowledge
is stored within them, they natu-
rally turn to teaching, writing
or speaking. They give out will-
ingly, but apparently are none
the poorer; their position in
the Uranus Line keeps them well
replenished,

In reality, this is a card
of the future. J C is a symbol of
the androgynous state toward which
the race is evolving. For that rea-
son the present manifestation is
often neutral-- a situation that
causes confusion and maladjustment
to present-day society. Many of the
women (especially) of these dates
fail to marry; the majority have
masculine minds and habits of life.
They are seldom domestic, never
"clinging vines" and have little
patience with pettiness or vanity.

For both sexes, the lack of
establishment on the side of so-
called normality causes them to
worry over their inability to make
prescribed adjustments and they
are apt to seek unusual attach-
ments which are unwise or discred-
iting-- as well as disappointing.
These they take very seriously;
their need for love is absorbing
and never quite satisfied. They
must cultivate good mental bal-
ance to steer clear of neuroses.
Their True Place-- Mars in the
Jupiter Line-- assures them of
protection if they work for it.

The only kind of work that
is congenial-- or endurable-- is
in the mental field, When they
are forced into menial tasks they
are unhappy and inefficient. They
must express themselves-- or suf-
fer. There is a terrific drive to
give out what they know and to
keep learning more and more. It
is a tragic thing when these peo-
ple are deprived of a good educa-
tion. They will add to the know-
ledge they have intuitively, no
matter what obstacles must be
overcome, but they are helped on
their way by a good educational
foundation,

Negatively, there is irres-
ponsibility, idle curiosity and
escapism into a multitude of un-
fortunate or discreditable by-
paths that are far removed from
the wisdom they have come to seek
and to preach.

They succeed best with an oc~
cupation that involves contacts.
People are highly important as
outlets for their abilities and
as companions to fill the gap of
their loneliness.

In the larger sense, J C is
the neophyte-- the young soul
seeking for wisdom, the inquirer
(or wanderer) who is full of un-
certainty between 18 and 30. They
are often skeptical and shifting
in beliefs; they can put their
knowledge to work for them or they
can live by their wits. They must
definitely establish themselves
between 30 and 60 if they are to
enjoy the remainder of their lives.
The close tie with the J D enables
them to do this successfully. The
ground on which they can rest with
security is the mental ground;
their weapon against all obstacles
is knowledge.

Bi

Jan, 29.

Feb. 27.
Pisc.

-165-
lenge for the J C
FEAR OF ESTABLISHED WISDOM
Ruled _b Cc

Ruler- Uranus

Born with occult know-

ledge. Will succeed if

they like their work-- not
otherwise. Good knack for
handling people. Humanitari-
an and enjoy helping others.
Can reach a high place as
writers, scientists, philoso-
phers or government officials,
More attracted to these lines
or to lecturing and teaching
than to business.

Ruler- Neptune

Restless and inclined to
discontent. Need contacts

and variety. Not good at rou-
tine jobs. Fine promoters, re-
ceptionists, interviewers.
Great mixers-- in any society.
Inclined to a mental career--
writing, poetry, journalism--
but often have talent for mu-
sic or acting. Very socially
minded. Become depressed when
shut up with their own famil-
ies or deprived of active oc-
cupation. Interested in in-
vestments-- property, oil, etc.

25.Ruler- Mars.

Speedy in movement, ner-
vous-- or touchy~-~ in re-
actions. Often feel "put upon"
or "unlucky". Have a tendency
to shift blame to others. Are
fine arguers and debaters but
apt to become quarrelsome. Do
not make adjustments easily
or optimistically. Strong per-
sonalities; influential as
writers, agitators, speakers.
Want a voice in what goes on.
May have some outstanding tal-
ent-- even genius; if the lat-
ter, are stormy and erratic,
difficult in private lives.
Valuable people when they use
balance and control.

Apr. 23.
Tau.

May 21.
Tau. or
Gen.

June 19.
Gem.

Ruler-- Venus.
Self-concerned and self-
indulgent. Have trouble
(women especially) with the
opposite sex, Health may be
a problem. Willing to work
hard for objectives-- espe~
cially in art or music. In-
terested in politics and al-
ways dramatize their part in
it. In-laws apt to present
problems. Want a home of
their own-- and dominate it.
Must watch the "rule or ruin"
tendency sometimes found in
Taurus. Attracted to theatre
or pictures. CAN be good ru-
lers or leaders.

Ruler-- Venus or Merc,

The Taureans make fine
actors, playwrights or
directors. Good livers and
spenders; good entertainers.
Gemini natives are more gift
ed in writing, (journalism or
editing), teaching and sell-
ing. Need a fast-moving occu-
pation. Fine lawyers (trial).
Slow to reach maturity and
always remain young. Good
linguists. Both keep late
hours. Both have many friends
and admirers among the oppo-
site sex. The Gemini born
take their loves lightly.
Ruler- Mercury.

Restless and dissatisfied
but more practical than

the other Gemini birthdate.
Always some problem connect-
ed with love or marriage. A
karmic date, demanding phil-
osophy and understanding--
which they often lack. Home
important but often live al-
one or share it with one who
is not congenial. Want mar-
riage for what it will give
them; take a job for what it
will pay. Should cultivate a
sense of service. Not favored
for journeys or investments.
Good brains, good writers,
speakers or actors.

## Page 171

JACK OF DIAMONDS

Diamonds - Values.

iD - 1) The Trader-- for Materi-

al Gain.
2) The Worker who lays up
Treasure in Heaven.
ll in D - Inspirational Guidance
in all Values.

The Neptune Card in the Uranus L,
Displaces the 3 S in the Nat. Sp.

The nature, disposition, pro~
clivities and qualities represent-
ed by this card take the prize for
variety and peculiarity. J D is
wholly material, highly spiritual
or a curious and incomprehensible
mixture of the two.

If they are operating direct-
ly under their own Birth Card,
they are well aware that hard and
continuous work is a requirement
for success; the displaced 3 S is
their assurance for that. They are
ready to sell anything for money
or value~- and some there are who
will sell their own birthright.
They want money and always find a
way to get it; they are mentally
keen, sharp and clever and are al-
ways looking for the thing that
pays off. Spiritually they are in-
variably confused. They want their
own kingdom but have not reached
the stage where they can assume
kingship. If opportunities for
gain are not at hand, they will
wander off to foreign lands and
keep a sharp lookout as they go--
or will drift through life and
live by their wits-- usually man-
aging to get by.

Their entire Sequence is in
the Neptune Line which always al-
lows a choice between idealism and
confusion. The cards in that Line
offer stability and power-- and we

seldom find a J D who lacks money
and protection, The Birth Card it-
self-- a Uranus- Neptune conjunc-
tion-- gives free play to the in-
tuitions (for good or bad) and an
unparalleled chance for spiritual
illumination; when they realize
it and accept it they are well on
their way to the kingly state.
When their fixed ideas (J) get in
the way, their material affairs
may still flourish but their spir-
itual security is lost for this
incarnation.

We find many who make valua-~
ble contributions along spirit-
ual and humanitarian lines. In
the case of men, it is most like-
ly that they are operating under
the King and have earned the right
to their crown. The women would
do better to stick to their Birth
Card and avoid the emphasis on the
Personality (Q) with its diffi-
cult Sequence.

The majority of these natives
love the sea; many of the men fol-
low it as a profession-- but even
if they make their start as deck
hands, they often, by "trading",
end by owning the ship.

They must have a profession
that is productive; they must al-
so have an outlet for their rare
gifts of originality and creation.
They are top executives in busi-
ness, diplomatic agents and go-
betweens, successful bankers, pub-
lishers and advertisers. Once they
learn how to judge values they are
indispensable to progress.

There is often difficulty in
choosing the right profession, The
idea that it must lead to financi-
al success may block the expres-
sion of a great talent.

Jan. 16.

Cap.

Feb. 14.
Aquar.

Mar.

12,

Apr. 10.

-169-

es Ruled by e

Ruler- Saturn

Good, practical sense of
values. Associated with
important business as offi-
cer or executive. If working
under the King, will command
a high salary. May get into

a rut because of the securi-
ty of their pesition. Travel
in the interests of others,
but have a voice in the de-
cisions. Good government of-
ficials-- especially ambassa-
dors-- or high-ranking offi-
cers in the armed forces--
especially naval.

Ruler- Uranus.

Attracted to the theatre

as actors or playwrights.
Good musical or dramatic crit-
ics-- but seldom kindly ones.
Women may be drifters, idlers
or opportunists. Many are con~
scious of a message to be giv-
en. If drawn to metaphysics
should beware of psychism;
often open to invasion from
wrong forces. Restless; de-
pend on their personality to
win their way. Good writers.
Ruler- Neptune

Interested in spiritual
growth. Poets, idealists,
metaphysical teachers. Can
develop direct communication.
Always expressive. Interested
in fraternal and occult orders.
A strong card financially. Do
more good with their money
than the majority of J D.
Writers, composers, actors,
dancers. Also druggists, trav-
el agents (steamship), res-
taurant managers.

Ruler~ Mars.

Clever at investigation.
Interested in politics

and like to " manipulate " and
pull strings. Work well with
others-- usually with a per-
sonal motive. Know the ropes

May 8,
Tau.

June 6,
Gen.

July 4.
Can.

Aug. 2.
Leo.

and can use them. Good promo-
ters. Know how to use money
effectively. Fluent speakers
and writers. Keenly observant.
Ruler- Venus.

Writers, poets, civic lead-
ers (political), realtors

and wholesalers. Always have
money and want more, Succeed
in working with the ground--
oil drilling, cultivated acre-
age or building and contract~-
ing. Ambitious for big busi-
mess and recognized leadership.
Protective of family and per-
sonal interests, Usually have
an artistic or musical hobby.
Ruler- Mercury.

Scientists, lawyers, edu-
cators, journalists. Good
mixers, good talkers. Person-
al contacts bring the best
results for business. Like to
sell articles and equipment
for home use. Interested in
communications-- telegraph,
telephone, radio, etc. Often
operators. Like home better
than travel.

Ruler- The Moon

Must work hard for results.
Like travel but can't al-
ways manage it. Deal in pub-
lic utilities, food, home ac-
cessories, soda fountains, ba-
keries, etc. Torn between a
desire for responsibility and
an urge for escape thro trav-
el. Good teachers of adults.
Ambitious for leadership.
Ruler- The Sun

Actors, novelists, commen-
tators, playwrights can
succeed with this date. Make
good also at banking, trading,
imsurance and physical cul-
ture. Like to be their own
bosses and make money through
their own efforts. Can always
make money by working but pre-
fer devising systems for get-
ting it with more speed and
less effort.

ence 2

Intelligence is a natural
gift-- and an inner convic-
tion that knowledge is power.
The majority want a good edu-
cation and will work for it.
Many are aware that "know-
ledge comes but wisdom stay's"
and wisdom is the goal they
are after. Few meet with se-
rious obstacles in youth and
if they are bent on obtain-
ing a good education, they
will acquire it. Spiritual in-
sight develops early.

Home life is important but
not always easy or pleas-

ant because of the many obli-
gations connected with it.
There is stability-- but also
the possibility of getting
into a rut unless they keep
active and progressive. Mar-
riage may be disappointing
because of a conflict of ob-
jectives. Friends are loyal
and helpful.

Work well with others--es-
pecially with groups of men.
They soon find their place as
“older brothers" and are at-
tracted to groups and clubs
whose objectives are render-
ing service to the human fam-
ily. They are good planners
and good executives; usually
follow a well-defined and
carefully laid out course.
Business is usually based
upon friendly contacts and
help from friends can always
be counted on. They can sell
their wares or themselves by
a friendly approach. Love is
important and they are bless-
ed when they have the devo-
tion of one person upon whom
they can rely.

This is an inheritance

card. Often have money

they have not earned at their
disposal. Success may be de-

=e
me

Birthdate

Jan. 3.
Cap.

Feb. 1,
Aquar.

layed through ill health,
but any work connected with
health is sure to succeed,
Make fine doctors.

Have a gift for handling
people and can depend on
loyalty from employees. The
more developed their intui-
tional power, the more suc~
cessful they become, Real
estate is especially favor-
ed, also big business and im-
portant corporations.

Have a keen interest in
foreign lands and people--
from personal attraction as
well as a cosmic obligation.
Travel is agreeable and sat-
isfactory. Love interests
are often involved with it.
The latter days are usually
in line with the heart's de~
sire.

CHOICE OF OBJECTIVES
Rule: S

Ruler- Saturn

Must overcome materialism--
also personal ambition for
the limelight. Despite their
marked ability as writers,
scientists and physicians, a
great many of these natives
are attracted to the stage or
pictures and acquit themselves
well. The Birthday Number

aids them in expression; the
Sign and its Ruler give them
seriousness and application.
Ruler- Uranus,

Even more theatre folk are
found in this birthdate--

as is usual for Aquarius, Here
is more emotional power, more
individuality and a keener
sense of progress as a part of
the new order. These are spe-
cialists in their chosen field--
acting, music, writing or sci-
ence,

## Page 177

QUEEN OF HEARTS

Hearts - Love.
Qu - A Magnet for Family and
Friends.
12 in H - Love and Justice toward
the Human Family.

The Neptune Card in the Neptune L,
Displaces the 10 S in the Nat. Sp.

This is a Card of beauty, mag-
netism, affection and idealism.
Inherent in it is so much that is
wanted and needed in the world, it
is almost a pity to have to men-
tion the faults and pitfalls that
are expressed in the lives of its
natives. The women represent the
much-loved mother, the sweetheart,
the indispensible sister or the
adored daughter. The men are gen-
tle, sensitive and creative, sym-
pathetic and understanding. If we
did not always have that inevita-
ble negative to deal with, this
would be the most desirable Card
in the Little Book.

The women are invariably at-
tractive, with a strong appeal to
the opposite sex. When they trade
on it they are flirts; they want
constant flattery, good clothes
and good times; they may become
lazy, frivolous and whiners.

The men may easily be too
gentle~- to the point of spine-
lessness, too self-indulgent, too
feminine, too unbalanced and sex-
ually indeterminate, The escapists
of both sexes have a drink prob-
lem to contend with.

All of them are popular and
hospitable, social-minded or cos-
mic-minded; cooperative and appre~
ciative; generous and faithful
(as a rule); just and honest. Al-
most invariably they are talented
in some artistic line; if they

cannot express in some art form
they listen and appreciate it.
They are intense and dramatic
and capable of deep devotion.

They are attracted to a pro-
fessional type of work or to mar-
riage. The women seldom make a
success of both at the same time.
Contacts are very important and
they should never live alone.
They are interested in foreign
lands and people and take them
to their hearts as readily as
their own. They are tolerant of
others’ customs, ideals and modes
of life, They are "shining" peo-
ple, optimistic, friendly and
comforting.

Even the undeveloped ones have
their charm and usefulness, for
though they may not be aware of
their potentialities or the im-
portance of their cosmic miss-
ion or their obligation as defin-
ed by their True Place (Saturn
Card in the Venus Line), they nev-
er willingly cause heartache or
distress and their flirtatious-
ness and triviality are harmless,

They have the privilege of
choice since they proceed direct-
ly to the Crown Row. They may fill
in the "blind spots" or may follow
the Sequence of their own pattern.
This, of course, applies only to
those whose Birth Card is actual-
ly the Q H-- not to the woman who
may choose to operate under it as
Personality.

They are impressionable and
receptive; many are psychic and
mediumistic. There is a strong
streak of religion in all of them.

Even when we should, we don't
like to find fault with them; they
are too loving and desirable.

Bir.

July 29.
Leo.

Aug. 27.
Vir.

-175-

uled by the Q H

Ruler- The Sun

Many of these people are
ardent reformers, sin-

cere religionists and unsel-
fish philanthropists-~ but
they all have exaggerated
egos and very nearly all

are megalomaniacs, They sim-
ply MUST be kings-- and woe
to the man (or woman) who
disputes their authority,
questions their opinions or
offends their ego! Those

who can work off this child-
ish complex in the theatre
(where many are found) or as
the head of some religious
or educational institution,
are easier to deal with in
social or family life; but
with the majority, those in
close association with them
must toe the mark-- or else!
They are too high-strung for
their own (or others') good.
Very successful musicians,
authors and merchants as
well as actors.

Ruler- Mercury

The least frivolous and
flirtatious of the Q H.
Mental and critical but will-
ing to see their own faults
as well as others’, Will sac-
rifice for a good education.
Forget themselves in working
for causes or digging for
facts. Good business managers
for others; efficient and ex-
ecutive. Writers, publishers,
philosophers. Overdo service.

Sept. 25,Ruler- Venus

Lib.

Often talented in art but
have more success as pa-
trons or dealers. Good judges
of quality and value. Collec-
tors, Good beauty operators.
Can succeed in law or polit-
ics. Exacting in family life.
Writers, dancers, poets. Are
fond of form and ceremony--
especially in religion.

Oct.
Lib.

Nov.
Scor.

Dec,
Sag.

23.

21.

19,

Ruler- Venus

(The last degree; may

be-- but rarely-- a Scor-
pio birthdate). The most
positive of the Q H. Stub-
born and impulsive. Demand
personal freedom, Retain
youthful appearance to old
age. Intuitional but incline
to materialism. Good govern-
ment officials, agents, law-
yers, salesmen. Love art but
cannot commercialize it. Are
successful in lines where
the personality counts. Dy-
namic and impressive. Not
well adapted for medicine.
Like to feel wanted and need-
ed. Very emotional,

Ruler~ Mars.

Mentally keen. Inclined

to suspicion. Disciplin-

ary toward others. May have
disturbing fears and doubts.
Borrow trouble; do not real-
ize their own capabilities.
Are better friends than mar-
riage partners. Should avoid
selfishness and self-pity,
Hard working and reliable as
employees, but want key po-
sitions. Suited to education-
al work, music, preaching,
government posts. Emotional
and religious,

Ruler- Jupiter

The most difficult date

of all QH. Suffer in the
emotional life; may have some
physical affliction to con-
tend with. Good recuperative
power and (usually) longliv-
ed. Hardships may be overcome
after maturity. Need a work-
ing philosophy to get by. Are
well suited to public life.
Mental and nervous. Attracted
to mechanics, science, radio
chemistry. Can succeed in bus-
iness but always approach ev-
erything from a scientific an-
gle. Discontented with them-
selves-- and others. Should
cultivate optimism,

equence the

If the business is fast~
moving or if in a profes-
sion, success comes quickly.
These natives size up people
and situations quickly. The
willingness to work is a re-
quisite for accomplishment,
but this Jupiter-Mercury com-
bination is a great asset.
May seriously consider mar-
riage in early years; if they
do not marry young, may not
at all; if they do, may mar-
ry again later on. Are just
as well off, usually, if they
avoid it.

Like to associate with

those of good brains and
quick wit. Subject to sudden
changes-- for good or ill.
Love may be a cross through
illness or disillusionment.
Often change their minds a-
bout what they really want--
or may have a fixed objective
and meet with delay in carry-
ing it through. Subject to
changes in the home-- travel
or removals. Like variety and
diversion and pursue it if
not too burdened by family
uncertainties.

Not sure of relations

with others. Have a sense

of insecurity about business
and the future. At certain pe-
riods in the life there is a
tenseness or limitation about
money. Need security and will
seek it. Usually manage to
hit on something that is pro-
ductive and that gets them
out of a rut. Apt to have two
or more irons in the fire at
the same time. A choice is
difficult and experiments are
made before finally deciding.
There is a strong desire

for occult manifestation.

All QC have a "brought-over"
knowledge of these laws and
the majority want to know how

alg
a
na

to apply it. When their
knowledge is used to attract
money, the results are un-
fortunate. Sensitive about
their own affairs. Business
interests or connections may
be involved with sickness.
Many become fine physicians.
Suffer through the injus-
tice or imposition of oth-
ers, Easily defrauded. Lose
money through taking the ad-
vice of friends or through
loans. May be hampered by a
concealed illness; should a-
void overwork, Must guard a-
gainst a tendency to jeal-
ousy, possessiveness and a
desire to dominate.

Want to own their own

home; always interested

in investments in real est-
ate, mines, etc-- but are
apt to lose money if the ven-
ture is at all speculative.
Keenly interested in metaphy-
sics. Will spend freely for
courses of study, equipment
and anything that contrib-
utes to the value of their
business. Will deprive them-
selves to supply their work
with the best tools. Are im-
patient with inefficiency in
employees; work hard them-
selves and dislike paying wa-
ges to loafers.

If they have not been a-

ble to accumulate money,
work may become burdensome in
the later years. Want travel
and changes but cannot always
indulge in them. Often need
rest and relaxation instead
of work. May change the occu-
pation or location after 50.
Usually more protected by
love and companionship late
in life than earlier,

#179=

Ruler- The Moon

A karmic birthdate. Are
usually interested in a
humanitarian cause, Should

be in public life, before

the footlights or writing on
subjects that concern public
interests or welfare. Must
guard against selfishness--
also narrowness in viewpoint.
Fine journalists and commen-
tators, novelists or histori-
ans. Need a good education.
Many study law as a step to
politics. May have a strong
religious bent. Interested

in cults and philosophies,
Ruler- The Sun.

More mental than the maj-
ority of Leo natives. Ve~

ry keen for money and like to
take chances to win it. Usu-
ally successful. Want to be
leaders-- and may overreach
themselves. Wonderful people
if developed. Restless. If in
the theatre, should try for
road engagements. Good at buy-
ing and selling. Attracted to
the opposite sex but uncertain
about their love affairs. Not
always happy in marriage. Are
creative in mental fields.

Sept, 12,Ruler- Mercury.

Vir.

Excellent technicians--

in art or the laboratory.
Mental and practical. Good in
journalism, architecture, bot-
any-- any science. Technical
lawyers, corporation counsel-
ors. Not interested in the
earth (farming, etc) except
for chemical analysis of soil
or experiments with plants.
Not easy or fluent writers or
speakers but interested in
literature. Can succeed as
publishers or advertisers.
Have a keen judgment of lit-
erary merit and business me-
thods. Good theoretical psy-
chologists~- not counselors.

Oct, 10, Ruler- Venus,

Lib.

Nov.
Scor,

Dec.
Sag.

8.

6.

Gifted as artists, ac~

tors and composers. Are
restless and ambitious. Not
often contented until they
reach the top. Demand per-
sonal freedom. If willing

to submit to training may be-
come important lawyers or
leaders in their special
field. Less soft and amen-
able than the majority of
Librans, May be prolific
writers-- especially on re-
ligion or philosophy. Are
seldom domestic. If disap-
pointed in love, will make
no effort to re-build.

Ruler- Mars.

Productive and executive,
Good financiers, heads

of corporations, insurance
brokers. Dramatic and magnet~
ic. Hard to convince, but
when they are, become ardent
converts-- and go too far.
Often have a sense of import~
ance that is ill-founded. If
talented in any line, will
work to reach the top-- and
mow down anything that stands
in the way. May easily become
ruthless. Intense and dynamic
in whatever course they follow.
Ruler- Jupiter.

A cosmic card. Interested

in humanity. Fine teach-
ers-~ especially of metaphys~
ics. Have unseen protection
in work but lack security in
their personal lives. Money
usually a problem; must work
hard for what they get. Eag-
er for knowledge-- to pass
on. Will spend for classes
rather than for home or self.
Connected with health prob-
lems; burdened with responsi-
bility. If undeveloped will
be crafty and secretive. Are
mental, nervous and sensi-
tive. Know they must serve.

Sequence f the QD Sat.

Attitudes and feelings

change frequently-- also

the home location or the de-

sire for travel. Restlessness

makes them want to leave home

early and establish themselves
elsewhere. Incompatibility

with family may contribute to
discontent. There is a certain
financial security in early

life which is not so dependa-

ble later on. A tendency to

fickleness should be checked.
Difficulty and uncertainty

about choosing friends, en-

vironment and career, Want to Uran.
associate with people of intel- 5D
ligence but oppose their ideas
and opinions. Disturbed if are
unable to put up a good appear-
ance. Will make sacrifices

for loved ones and carry their
burdens.

Will work hard for a good
salary, even though the

work may be distasteful. May
get into a rut for fear any
change might result in less in-
come. Should avoid legal mat-
ters unless the situation is
well defined, Always uncertain
about work~associates. The wom-
en should never go into busi-
ness with their husbands or as-
sist in their offices. Prob-
lems are sure to result.
Technically, this card

means "loss of time in the
pursuit of happiness"-- even
though, in prediction parlance,
it is the "wish" card. There
is not much chance for Jupiter-
ian blessings in emotional
lines that involve close rela-
tionships. Friends may be re-
liable and helpful-- but they
are also likely to be expens~
ive. Have difficulty in rais-
ing money when needed, Will
help others but cannot help
themselves. Uncontrollable cir-
cumstances present obstacles.

ole
wy
n

Illnesses are often in-
duced by worry. A7 C

person would be helpful in
case of trouble. There is e-
nough money behind them but
it is not always available.
It is well to bear in mind
the meaning of the 7 C. If
its underlying principles are
followed, many of the diffi-
culties are surmounted. It is
wise to keep away from the at~
mosphere of illness whenever
possible-- no nursing or med-
ical career. The study of met-
aphysics will solve many prob-
lems.

Business interests are of-
ten at a distance. Trav-

el may be helpful. Can buy or
sell land or property for a
quick turnover. Restless in
the given occupation and want
to change it-- but often re-
main where they are for fear
of risk. The overcoming of
worry contributes to business
success. May make ill-advised
changes; should weigh all an-
gles carefully-- but avoid
remaining in a position that
offers no chance for growth.
The later years may be in-
fluenced by a woman who

is hard-working, executive
and an extensive traveler. May
marry late in life one who is
a world-traveler or who has
achieved a measure of fame--
or may travel for such a per-
son. There is more security
in finances than in earlier
life; may even acquire or in-
herit considerable wealth.
This is a better card for a
woman than a man. In the case
of the men, there is apt to
be domination.

## Page 187

EEN _OF SPADES

Spades -~- Labor; Wisdom.
- The "Crown" of Labor.
12 in S - Organization of Service
to Humanity.

The Mercury Card in the Uranus L.
Displaces the 10 D in the Nat. Sp.

Together with the QC, this
card represents cosmic motherhood.
These two Q's are the Mary and
Martha of the Bible. The QC sits
at the feet of the Teacher that
she may learn; the Q S runs His
household and smooths His pathway
that the Source of Wisdom may
enrich the world unhampered. Both
of these cards are closely connec-
ted with the 10 D; both are cen-
ters in the Divine Plan-- the QC
as center of the Natural Spread
the Q S as center of the Crown
Line. For the QS this is often
the source of her troubles,

Q S people have come to lead
and direct; they are co-rulers
with the highest authority-- the
KS. When they find themselves in
a subordinate position, it is gal-
ling and irksome to them for they
know they do not belong there.
That, however, is exactly what hap-
pens to those who are operating
negatively. They symbolize the

household drudges, caretakers,
janitors or menial servants of
the world. They work hard and
are ill paid, they live "down

to earth"=- ignorant of true val-
ues, incapable of intelligent
judgment, lacking in vision, des-
pairing of the future. They are
high-strung, nervous, jealous
and antagonistic-- and usually
mercenary.

Even among those who are aw-
are of their supremacy, there is
a conflict as to how it shall be
expressed and it often results
in a dictatorial attitude and dis-
ciplinary insistence when it comes
to dealing with others.

They have good mental balance,
right judgment of values, and ea-
gerness for service and a willing-
ness to work without sparing them-
selves. They know where they be-
long and they are continually
struggling to get back to the
"Crown',

They are usually in business
for themselves and will hire any-
thing they dislike to do. They
are excellent managers for others.
Intuitive, impulsive and indepen-
dent, they are valuable contribu-
tors to the highest type of accom-
plishment.

PASAT ATASACATASAG
Planetary Sequence for the Q S$ Ven. The women like to spend
9D money on the home; the

Merc. Quick minds and ready
Jc learners. The early life
is often influenced by the

men want an impressive off-
ice. Love affairs-- and of-
ten marriage-- are disap-

attitude of the father or ol-
der brother. Restless and in-
quiring, they are apt to make
many experiments before set-
tling on a-career, They usu-
ally recognize the necessity
for mental training.

pointing and expensive, Mar-
riages go to pieces over fi-
nancial difficulties. Many
do not marry at all. Should
not lend money to friends if
they expect to collect it.
May develop penuriousness.

## Page 189

13 KINGS 13

R wes symbolize the positive,
masculine, activating prin-
ciple in humanity; they rep-

resent aggressiveness as initia-

tive-- not combativeness. They
are endowed with authority and
rulership but their number in the

Little Book indicates that they

have not sole authority. Between
their 1 and 3 stands 2, the moth-
er or the Queen, Before initia-
tive (1) is expressed (3), it
must be nurtured, formulated and
given a body as principle. The
Kings, therefore, although they
occupy the highest place are but
co-rulers, like the Queens. With-
out the spiritual vision, fur-
nished by the Queens, their "peo-
ple" would "perish",

13 by reduction is 4-- the
builder of the foundation and
the layer of the cornerstone.
There are 4 of these Kings and
4 x 13 or 52 is the number of
"pages" in the Little Book. In
any 4 there is always a poten-
cial 22-- the Master Magician,
the transformer of ideals into
realities,

As with the natives of these
cards, mystery and misconception
(as well as negative or evil ex-
pression) have been built around
the number, 13 is the number of
two Hebrew words-- Love and Unity
-- and among the wiser ones of old,
these qualities together with
their number, were held to be sa-
ered. It is only a Christian su-
perstition, derived from the trag-
ic deflection of Judas, that gives
to 13 the label evil or "unlucky".
In the lives of many of our "Kings"

the harmful superstition has done
its work, since we invariably and
inevitably express what is built
into our consciousness.

Kings are the Jacob of the
Bible-- the founders and fathers
of the 12 (tribes) who were en-
trusted with leading the "chil-
dren" to the Source of All Good.
In the Hebrew Liturgy there were
13 logical rules for interpreting
the law and this is actually the
task of the Kings of the 4 suits.

Kings are usually kindly peo-
ple, sympathetic and understand-
ing. In the Sequence they may re-
present the father or an older
brother, not a son.

They know subconsciously

that their power depends upon co-
operation; in whatever line they
follow their best work is done in
partnership. They always have a
sense of authority but it seldom
leads to domination. If operating
negatively they can be very antag-
onistic and quarrelsome.

HEARTS rule by love. They are
pleased when their deeds
bring blessings but they
let others take the glory.

CLUBS wield their power through
knowledge. They know that
mind-development is the
surest road to progress.

DIAMONDS “have dominion" over all
"substance", Theirs is
the power of distribution.

SPADES rule by wisdom. They are
the guardians of Divine
Law, initiates who have
earned their crowns,

ence ie K H

There is a conflict here

between heart and brain.

These people are not sure Sat.
whether their feelings should Js
be allowed to dominate or
their common sense. Due to in-
decision, they may allow them-
selves to be influenced by
the wrong person. If they go
into business early, it will
be with some one who has suf-
ficient means to finance it.
If a woman, she will marry a
man who has money or is con-
nected with law, politics or
large groups.

To all K H peace of heart

is the most desirable thing 8c
on earth. They want security
in surroundings but more than
that, they want security in
love-- and they want it to
last forever. They keep their
friends a long time and are
never responsible for breaks
if they occur, This is the
card that is allied to the
Christ Principle and that is
the platform upon which they
stand in their relationships.
Mentally active and carry

it into their work. They

are thoroughly efficient and
practical in business. They
like to mix with men and en-
joy an exchange of ideas. The
desire to study and learn is
strong but they do not always
apply what they know. They
want books around and may be
encyclopaedias of stored-up
knowledge-~ and do nothing
about it.

Interested in partnerships
-- especially where money is
involved. Amenable to the i-
deas and suggestions of oth-
ers. They like trading, mer-
chandizing, buying and sell-
ing. Work well with large
manufacturing concerns, also

oe
Io
]

with personnel. They want

a business that is progress~-
ive and active but are not
agreeable to drastic changes.
Problems are presented by
people who are irresolute

or self-indulgent. May be
drawn into the wrong company
through such an influence.

If attracted to medicine,
will become a leader in that
field. Will enjoy training
or working with a doctor who
is advanced in his profession.
For the sake of sound health
these people should avoid
carelessness in diet and late
hours. They need much sleep.
This card always endows

with power through know-
ledge. In the Uranus posi-
tion intuitional gifts are
added. There is a strong in-
clination to spiritual devel-
opment; they instinctively
are attracted to metaphysics,
May become spiritual or phil-
osophical teachers. Want to
give out their knowledge to
those less instructed than
themselves. Good leaders and
teachers of groups.

Despite their desire to
think straight and judge
correctly, these people are
often confused in their sense
of values. They know they
must pay all debts but are
disturbed about their karmic
obligations. They often re-
gard their problems as evi-
dence that they have not met
them. They suffer from disap~
pointment in themselves, The
latter days are secure but
may seem monotonous to some
of the Birthdates. There are
few journeys or changes but
if they travel to a foreign
country they will remain a
long time. Long journeys for
the sake of travel prove dis-
appointing,

## Page 193

Clubs ~ Knowledge.

Ke - Maturity in Knowledge.

13 in C - Discrimination and Bal-
ance in Knowledge.

The Uranus Card in the Uranus L.
Displaces the 2 S in the Nat. Sp.

This is a card of ripe judg-
ment. Kings have passed through
the various tests imposed and are
equipped for control of the field
assigned to them and the ability
to pass on to others the results
of their training.

By nature, K C are spiritually
minded, although forceful and of-
ten hasty and aggressive. When
their knowledge is applied on the
higher levels they become physi-
cians or spiritual healers. When
they are chary of their gifts and
inclined to barter or debase then,
they become hard and self-center-
ed, unsympathetic and incapable of
rendering service to others or of
achieving any further growth for
themselves.

By position, the type of know-
ledge inherent in these people is
mot only of the conscious mind or
efficient brain but is also occult
in character. Uranus opens doors
of understanding and when there is
@ power card in that position, we
have only to walk through the door
and discover for ourselves what
lies on the other side.

The True Place-- Saturn in
the Jupiter Line-- bespeaks the ob-
ligation to act as Teacher and
Counselor and the mutual blessing
(Jupiter) to be derived therefrom.
The displacement of the 2 S in-
clines these people to business,
preferably in association. Two al-
ways involves union, agreements,

LUBS

dickering, discussing and exchang-
ing ideas. There is always much
detail connected with their work--
papers, messages, records and da-
ta and among the very successful,
when struggle has become a thing
of the past, there is danger of
getting into a rut of routine or
static prosperity because of the
two 6's at the end of the Sequence.
These people are meant to be in- .
defatigably progressive and they
must take care that they live up
to the expectation. When they de-
tect any signs of over-content-
ment or self-sufficiency, they
should give themselves a swift
prod and a strong "shot" in the
name of progress. The Club symbol,
it must be remembered, is the up-
ward-pointing clover.

As a rule, both sexes are
keen in learning and quick think-
ers. The women, however, are of-
ten guilty of scattering their
forces because of emotional dis-
turbance or family problems. They
succeed best if happily married
and can be of great help to their
husbands by furnishing workable
ideas or by active participation
in the mental angles of their
business. Both sexes are strong
for family ties; they make excel-
lent parents and will make sacri-
fices to provide their children
with a good education.

Even the careless and nega-
tive among them have keen intel-
ligence and insight although they
often waste themselves in idle cu-
riousity instead of a quest for
knowledge that counts and there-
fore never attain the high place
of power that is theirs by right.
It is these Kings collectively,
however, that lead us to a know-
ledge of the why and wherefore of
our being. They are the Knowers.

## Page 197

KING OF

Diamonds - Values.

KD ~- Judgment based on Mate-
rialism,

13, in D - Occult Understanding of
Values.

The Venus Card in the Mars L.
Displaces the 3 C in the Nat. Sp.

The accepted interpretation
of this card is most uncomplimen-
tary, but there are so many glar-
ing exceptions in the conduct of
its natives, they should be stress~
ed even more emphatically than
the "run of the mill".

K D people are victims of the
materialistic trend that has char-
acterized our evolution for hun-
dreds of years. Since we have set
money as our goal and standard,
what can its custodians do but
fight to acquire it, manipulate
it and prove themselves efficient
rulers and controllers of it?
What, indeed, UNLESS they are in
touch with the mighty Uranian
force that is granted them in
their True Place-- Jupiter in the
Uranus Line?

As in the case of the majori-
ty of Diamond natives, the bas-
ic error lies in the definition
of Values. If we are born to pow-
er, being Kings, we must equip
ourselves for rulership-- and if
power means money-- and only that,
money we must get in such abund-
ance that no one can outstrip us
or outdo us. It is no wonder
that only a very few accept and
work on the principle so clearly
defined in the Great Book-- "Not
by might nor by power, but by My
Spirit" saith the Lord of Hosts.
Those who do are the initiates;
the hard-boiled materialism of

NDS.

the typical K D is unknown to them.
As politicians they refuse to ac-
cept bribes; as business men they
are never ruthless-- overriding
the little fellow with the little
business or exacting from him the
grilling bonus or hush-money as
the only means of his continuance
to function and support his fam-
ily; as "joiners" they do not use
their club or fraternity to fea-
ther their own nests; as corpora~
tion heads they do not contrive
and connive until they get cont-
rol of the stock and are able to
proclaim a freeze-out for their
fellow-directors.

When not operating strictly
on the negative side, they are suc~
cessful business people who must
always watch out for the tendency
to grab the surplus but who are
willing to take gamblers' chances
because they can afford to lose--
but seldom do. They are never in
inferior positions; they always
have ample funds at their dispo~
sal-- or backers who will come to
their rescue. They are always king-
pins and top dogs.

The women are more undecided
but always positive in action; they
have the troublesome Q D to handle
and unless they keep their person-
alities out of all business deal-
ings, they will meet with emotional
disappointment and frustration.

Positively, the K D are endow-
ed with wisdom and occult power.
They may appear cold and hard-- but
at heart they are strictly just
and inclined to philanthropy; much
depends upon the birth Sign and
Number. With true spiritual devel-
opment, the negative traits may
never manifest. They all have the
power of accumulation and control,

## Page 200

Spades - Labor; Wisdom.

KS - The Highest Initiate.

13.in 5 - High Spiritual Voltage
in Practical Application.

The End Card in the Crown Line.
No Displacement - a Fixed Card.

The K S is the "highest" of
all the cards, yet it produces
many mediocre prople and quite a
few failures. A few hundred years
from now that will probably not
be the case; we shall have learn-
ed better how to handle "high spir-
itual voltage", what sort of ob-
ligation we are under when entrus-
ted with a mission and just what
it means to become an initiate.

Some of these people are big
enough to meet their opportunities
and make the grade. Through suffer-
ing and the hard road to wisdom
they have taken their degrees up
to the final one-- Rulership.
They have power because they have
earned it, but they are too wise
in humility to flaunt or abuse it.
Because they don't talk about it
they are called secretive; because
they don't brag about it, it is
often not recognized and because
they are preachers and teachers
of the great truths of resurrec~
tion, re-birth and eternal life
they are called fanatics or crack-
pots.

When these Spades have actu~
ally reached the King stage, it
matters not at all to them what
they are called or how they are
treated, The K S has no alter-
nate; he is fixed and immovable,
displacing nothing but himself,
free to move to any Line or Posi-
tion in the Spread for more effec-
tive operation and never separated
from his great wisdom or high crown.

SPADE!

He knows the Law for he is
the embodiment of all the laws.
He is misunderstood because he is
dealing with things of which the
majority are as yet ignorant.

In the Natural Order he comes
directly to the A H-- a desire for
love-- but since this card is dis-
placed by the 3 H in the Mundane
Spread, his emotional life will be
disturbed by uncertainty in rela-
tionships and unreliability in his
closest association.

These people are seldom suc-
cessful in marriage because of
this emotional conflict, always
disturbing to the required regula-
tion of the mental attitudes. If
marriage is not entered into early
in life, there is likely to be no
marriage at all but rather an in-
crease in the population of nun-
neries, monasteries, ashrams or
other types of holy or secret or-
ders. A cloistered life is often
voluntarily chosen as one of the
disciplines of personal denial or
the advantages of spiritual refuge.

Many remain in the world and
very much of it, They are person-
ally ambitious, self-protective,
capable of living and enjoying
life to the fullest-- like other
kings or commoners. They may not
go far in terms of their high call-
ing, but they manage to leavs an
imprint in their chosen line and
seldom sink to lowness or meanness
or deliberate evil,

When we meet a real teacher
whose birthdate is January lst
(the only date that is ruled by
this card) we shall be wise indeed
if we sit at his feet and get all
the instruction he is willing to
give us. We are on holy ground.

deep esoteric meaning behind the
"Joker" of our playing cards, the
foolish little fellow at the bot-
tom of the page would seem to have
not the slightest relation to the
"Fool" of the Tarot.

The initiate-teachers of old
deliberately concealed much of
their priceless wisdom from the
"profane" by words or pictures
which conveyed opposite or dis-

The "Joker" natives are a
law unto themselves. They
belong in the "Crown Line"
as much as do the other 3.
The wise ones choose their
own birthdays. They can

torted meanings to all but the
serious students who, by medita-
tion and visual impression, could
see behind the veil and discover
the truth.

The Foolof the Tarot is the
pictorial statement of the One
Force, the NO THING (0) yet Ev-
erything to all men--Eternal En-
ergy, boundless, measureless and
infinite. It is all seasons, all
forms and all activities.

The Fool of the Little Book
is, for some players, the "high-
est trump"; for the majority it
is discarded and forgotten. It
is, however, included as the "0"
page, for its inescapable symbo-
lism represents the complete mo-
tion of the earth about the Sun
and is the sole accountant for
the "remnant of days" in our so-
lar year. (See page 1). It, too,
is all seasons; it is the 4 quar-
ters of the earth-- the 4 Suits,
therefore all Cards and all Birth-
dates-- "all things to all men".

As a single card, it rules
but one birthdate, December 31st,
the first decanate of Capricorn,
ruled by Saturn. Its natives are
indeed "all things to all men".

choose to operate as the K
S or the A H -- in the Plan,
not the Mundane Spread. It
is impossible to analyze
them; they hold the key to
themselves-- and guard it.
